---
title: "Donna Tartt — A Collector's Reference"
subtitle: "Every published work, edition, special issue, signed copy, and notable artifact"
scope: |
  This reference catalogues:
    (1) Works BY Donna Tartt — novels, short stories, essays, forewords, afterwords,
        introductions, contributed pieces, blurbs, translations, audiobook narrations,
        and any other published primary text she has authored.
    (2) Direct interviews with Tartt where she is the speaker — Q&A formats, recorded
        conversations, transcripts.
    (3) Editions, printings, signed copies, ephemera, and authentication aids for
        the above.

  This reference deliberately EXCLUDES:
    – Critical essays and academic scholarship about Tartt's work
    – Reviews of her books (whether positive, negative, or mixed)
    – Profile articles about Tartt that don't include direct quoted statements from her
    – Award announcements and prize news coverage
    – Anniversary retrospectives and commentary by other writers
    – Fan response, dark-academia trend pieces, and social-media discussion

  Such secondary material is useful biographical and cultural context but is not
  catalogued here.
---

## 1. About Donna Tartt

Donna Louise Tartt was born December 23, 1963, in Greenwood, Mississippi. She studied at Bennington College in Vermont between 1982 and 1986. Tartt has clarified that **her primary course of study at Bennington was philosophy** (per the §6.12 Il Foglio interview, 15 Sept 2025: *"Bennington, exclusive college del Vermont dove aveva deciso di studiare filosofia mentre Bret Easton Ellis e Jay McInerney approfondivano lo studio della letteratura"* — i.e., "where I had decided to study philosophy while Bret Easton Ellis and Jay McInerney were deepening their study of literature"). Earlier secondary-source biographies often add classics; her Bennington-era cohort included Ellis (dedicatee of *The Secret History*) and McInerney.

Three novels in three decades — *The Secret History* (Knopf, 1992), *The Little Friend* (Knopf, 2002), and *The Goldfinch* (Little, Brown, 2013) — form the core of her published work; *The Goldfinch* won the 2014 Pulitzer Prize for Fiction. Tartt has also published a small body of short fiction, nonfiction, and one documented translation (Rimbaud, §7.22, 2006); has narrated audiobooks (§2.10, §3.7, §4.13, §7.2); and has contributed introductions, forewords, afterwords, or essay contributions to several volumes by other writers — most prominently Charles Portis's *True Grit* (Bloomsbury, 2005 / Overlook, 2010; §7.1), Bonaventure's *Life of St. Francis* (HarperSanFrancisco, 2005; §7.23), Shirley Jackson's *We Have Always Lived in the Castle* (Folio Society, 2023; §7.14), and J.F. Martel's *Reclaiming Art in the Age of Artifice* (Counterpoint / Basic Books, 2024; §7.6). The ten-year gap between novels has been widely noted in the press; Tartt is private and rarely interviewed.

**Current status (per Il Foglio interview, 15 Sept 2025, §6.12):** Tartt is **actively writing her fourth novel**. She has sold her New York apartment and "retreated to write at a ranch in Virginia, not far from where her mother lives" (Tartt is "very close" to her mother). The Il Foglio interview is the first major Tartt-bylined public statement since the 2020 Portis tribute (§6.11) and the 2024 Harper's "Art and Artifice" essay (§6.5).

**Genealogical notes (compiled from the Tartt ABCs bibliographer project at @tartt-abc.bsky.social, 2024–2026):**

- **Surname history.** The doubled-t spelling "Tartt" is a relatively recent family addition. Henry Wesley Tart (1877–1958), a Tallahatchie County farmer, added the second 't' to the family surname at some point after 1940. Donna Tartt is therefore in the first generation born under the doubled-t spelling. This is useful as an authentication / forgery red flag — a signature with single-t "Tart" would be incorrect for Donna's own signature.
- **Grandmother (maternal line).** **Florence Louise Boushe** (30 Nov 1911 – 11 Aug 2012; Grenada, Mississippi). This is the grandmother — *distinct from* the "beloved great-grandmother" who features in §7.19 (Fairy Tale Review Blue Issue 2005 essay "On Barrie and Stevenson") and §7.24 (Burningham *When We Were Young* 2004 hummingbird-memory essay). The great-grandmother in those Tartt-authored essays was born in 1890.
- **Earliest documented public appearance (Tartt-as-subject ephemera, age 4).** *Clarion-Ledger* (Jackson, Mississippi), **17 June 1968**, p. 2: a notice of Donna Tartt onstage as **"Little Miss Grenada Lake of 1968-1969"** (via Newspapers.com; surfaced by the Tartt ABCs project). This predates by a year the earliest previously-catalogued Tartt-ephemera entry.
## 2. The Secret History (1992)

### 2.1 US first edition (Alfred A. Knopf, New York)

**Cover:** `assets/images/rId22.jpg` — `TSH-001` (US Knopf 1st/1st (acetate jacket))


![Figure 2.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st with the issued printed acetate jacket, dust-jacket showing the John Kerl photograph, $23.00 price on rear flap. Photo: Rare Book Cellar (T2)](assets/images/rId22.jpg "Figure 2.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st with the issued printed acetate jacket, dust-jacket showing the John Kerl photograph, $23.00 price on rear flap. Photo: Rare Book Cellar (T2)")

Figure 2.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st with the issued printed acetate jacket, dust-jacket showing the John Kerl photograph, $23.00 price on rear flap. Photo: Rare Book Cellar (T2)

*Figure 2.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st with the issued printed acetate jacket, dust-jacket showing the John Kerl photograph, $23.00 price on rear flap. Photo: Rare Book Cellar (T2)*

Bibliographic block

  - Publisher: Alfred A. Knopf, New York; distributed by Random House

  - Publication date: September 16, 1992 (Open Library / publisher record)

  - ISBN-10: 0-679-41032-5 (check-digit valid)

  - ISBN-13: 978-0-679-41032-4 (check-digit valid)

  - LCCN: 92-053053

  - OCLC: 26515217; LC class: PS3570.A657 S4 1992; Dewey 813/.54

  - Pages: 524

  - Format: octavo

  - Binding: original pictorial paper boards (NOT cloth); spine lettered black on white ground

  - Dust jacket: printed acetate (issued without a paper jacket); $23.00 price on rear flap

  - Jacket designers: Chip Kidd and Barbara de Wilde

First edition identification points

1. "First Edition" stated on copyright page; no later printing statement.

2. Pictorial paper boards — never issued in cloth at this printing.

3. Printed acetate dust jacket with $23.00 price on rear flap; jacket carries blurbs by John Grisham, Jay McInerney, and Ruth Rendell.

4. Spine lettered in black on white ground.

5. Jacket design credit: Chip Kidd and Barbara de Wilde.

The acetate jacket is fragile; copies routinely surface with chipped or rubbed jackets. Edges of the boards foxing lightly is common and forgivable in collectible copies; missing acetate is a significant defect.

Conservation note for the printed acetate jacket

The 1992 Knopf Secret History dust jacket is printed on cellulose acetate film, a material chemically distinct from paper or polyester (Mylar). Acetate has known long-term failure modes that affect a substantial fraction of surviving copies and warrant the collector's deliberate attention:

  - Edge cracking and chipping — the dominant defect; concentrated at the top spine fold and bottom corners. Even fine copies typically show some chipping; very-fine examples are scarce.

  - Yellowing — slow over decades; intensified by UV exposure. Store away from direct light.

  - Ink offset onto boards — the printed black titling can transfer onto the white ground of the boards under sustained pressure. A copy with offset ghost text on the front board is permanently devalued.

  - Vinegar syndrome — advanced acetate decomposition exhibits a sharp acetic-acid smell; copies showing this odour are deteriorating rapidly and the jacket is past saving.

  - Static electricity — acetate attracts dust; clean only with a soft cloth and avoid abrasive paper.

  - Sleeves — Brodart-brand polyester (Mylar) protective covers are the conservation standard; do not store acetate-jacketed copies in PVC sleeves (PVC plasticisers attack acetate over time).

  - Storage — vertical shelving with light pressure between books, climate-controlled (target 18–22°C, 40–55% RH), low-UV. Avoid attics, basements, and direct heat sources.

Repair work on chipped acetate jackets is generally NOT advisable for collectible copies — the material does not glue cleanly, and amateur intervention typically reduces value. Severe damage warrants a conservator (the Library of Congress Preservation Directorate maintains a Conservation Specialist Directory). For copies sold without the acetate jacket, the loss reduces value by 50–80%; the jacket is intrinsic to the issued state of this title.

Reported variants and states

Two cloth-tone variants — "yellow tone" and "gray tone" — are reported by fedpo.com (Tier 1.5) and the Biblio "Collecting" page (Tier 2 aggregator). Per fedpo, both tones are observed on first printings; fedpo additionally observes "the yellow tone on second printings, and based on this we believe that the gray tone preceeds [sic] the yellow tone."

The "shorter / glossy boards / black border" variant is confirmed via primary source. Per Lacey Books Ltd (Cirencester, UK) [Source: S091] listing for ISBN 9780679410324: "1992 Alfred A Knopf hardcover stated First Edition, first printing… This is a scarce variant printing of the first edition. The book and jacket are about 0.5cm shorter than the more common printing and the boards are glossy instead of matt with a 1.5cm black border extending around the cover image."

Print run and advance

Verbatim from Esther B. Fein, "THE MEDIA BUSINESS; The Marketing of a Cause Celebre," The New York Times, November 16, 1992, Section D, Page 6: "Knopf bought the book a few days before the 1991 American Booksellers Convention, which was held that year in New York City. People familiar with the negotiations said the publisher paid about $450,000 for the book, which was the highest offer Ms. Urban received, and paperback rights were sold for about $500,000 more to Ivy. In quick order, Alan J. Pakula bought the movie rights."

Other Fein-article facts: original working title "The God of Illusions"; publication date "early September" was chosen by Sonny Mehta to come before the traditional mid-fall release of big-name bestselling authors; Tina Brown commissioned the September 1992 Vanity Fair profile by James Kaplan after Urban told her at lunch in July 1992 that Tartt was "hot."

The widely-cited "75,000 first-printing print order" figure is NOT in the Fein article; that attribution is incorrect. The 75,000 print run is confirmed by contemporary Newsweek coverage: Laura Shapiro & Ray Sawhill, "Anatomy of a Hype," Newsweek, September 7, 1992 — "Most first novels get a first printing of about 10,000 copies; Tartt's is getting 75,000" (present tense, written at time of publication). This is a Tier 1 journalistic primary source. The figure is further echoed in the Southern Literary Review profile (Cameron Williams, 2012): "sold well over its initial print of 75,000 copies." A 1stDibs dealer description repeats the figure: "instead of the typical order of 10,000–20,000 copies, the publisher ordered 75,000 copies." The primary Fein NYT article documents the buzz and bestseller-list outcome but does not itself state the print run number; the Newsweek article is the confirmable primary source for the 75,000 figure. [Source: S080]

Corroborating ABAA dealer descriptions of signed and inscribed copies

6. Peter Harrington (ABA / ILAB / PBFA), Stock Code 177243 — inscribed "To Sandy — warmest regards, Donna Tartt"

7. Bauman Rare Books (ABAA), Item \#104963 (sold) — inscribed "To Ward, best wishes from Donna Tartt"

8. Second Story Books (ABAA), \#1393608 — inscribed "To Lanette — warm regards" (sans dust jacket)

9. Between the Covers Rare Books (ABAA) — briefly inscribed presentation copy

10. Grayshelf Books (ABAA / IOBA) — signed and inscribed to a local attorney and spouse

11. Collector variant — copies signed by Tartt and jacket designer Chip Kidd. First-edition/first-printing copies of TSH signed by both Donna Tartt and jacket designer Chip Kidd have appeared at Raptis Rare Books (raptisrarebooks.com). Three distinct copy-types are documented: (1) Presentation copy inscribed by Tartt on the half-title ('To Diana- warm regards- Donna Tartt') plus signed four times by Chip Kidd (front board, front dust-jacket panel, half-title page, rear jacket panel); Near Fine in a near fine price-clipped dust jacket; Raptis item 143517. (2) Boldly signed (not inscribed) by Tartt on the half-title plus signed four times by Chip Kidd at the same locations; Fine in a near fine dust jacket. (3) Signed three times by Chip Kidd only (no Tartt signature) on front board, half-title, and rear jacket panel; Fine in a near fine dust jacket. All three types carry the note 'Jacket design by Chip Kidd and Barbara De Wilde' (confirming the dual credit at Para 53 above). Described by dealer as 'Rare and desirable.'

**WorldCat:** [OCLC 26515217](https://www.worldcat.org/oclc/26515217).

### 2.2 US Knopf per-printing matrix (1st through 4th printings)
Book-club editions: TSH first printing of 75,000 (per PW Sept 2002 “Donna Tartt's Second Act”) included Book-of-the-Month Club (BOMC) and Quality Paperback Club (QPB) selections. Separate book-club identification points (different binding state, different copyright page wording, separate ISBN) are documented in collector market-lore tier but not pinned via primary-source dealer description. AbeBooks dealer descriptions for non-first printings trace to 5th, 6th, and 8th printings. BOMC identification criteria (fedpo.com Tier 1.5 + tomfolio.com general BOMC criteria): (1) No price printed on dust jacket rear panel — BOMC copies blank the retail price. (2) Barcode on rear panel: top-right digit block is blank or zeroed-out (trade copies carry full ISBN barcode with price extension). (3) BOMC blind stamp on rear board — a round or rectangular blind-stamped impression on the back board (early-1990s BOMC used both round and square stamps). (4) BOMC code printed sideways inside rear endpaper — a small alphanumeric club-identifier code in the gutter margin of the rear pastedown or free endpaper, typically rotated 90 degrees. (5) Endpaper color may differ: trade TSH first has colored endpapers; some BOMC copies reported with white endpapers, though this is not universal across all printings. QPB note: Quality Paperback Book Club is a paperback-only club; no hardcover QPB variant of TSH exists. Copies described as “QPB selection” are trade paperback reprints, not first-edition hardcovers. Identification criteria above are sourced from fedpo.com (Tier 1.5 TSH-specific) and tomfolio.com (general BOMC criteria).

Knopf moved fast on this title: the second printing was struck before the official September 16, 1992 publication date (this is unusual and indicative of advance demand from booksellers and reviewers). Identification statements per dealer descriptions:

| | | |
| --------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Printing** | **Copyright-page statement** | **Notes** |
| 1st printing | "First Edition" stated, no other printing line | Pub date 9/16/1992; the trade collectible state |
| 2nd printing (before publication) | "Second Printing Before Publication" stated | Printed before 9/16/1992 — anticipated demand. Some signed copies exist (e.g. Grayshelf Books ABAA listing — signed on half-title). |
| 3rd printing | "Third printing (September 1992)" stated | Same month as publication; demand-driven reprint |
| 4th printing | "Fourth printing, October 1992" stated | First post-publication reprint |
| 5th printing and later | Each carries explicit printing statement on copyright page | Per-printing dealer cataloguing thins out beyond 4th; Knopf reissued through the 1990s |

Collectibility falls off quickly past the first/first; the second printing (before publication) is sometimes mistaken for a first by inexperienced sellers — the explicit printing statement is the definitive disqualifier. A 1st-printing copy that has been clipped of its acetate jacket loses substantial value. Signed second-printing copies are uncommon enough to be an interesting niche collectible but are not first/firsts.

Later-printing jacket note: later undated Knopf hardcover printings of The Secret History were issued in a standard printed paper dustjacket — not the acetate film jacket of the first printing — and with plain (unprinted) boards rather than the first printing’s pictorial paper boards. A copy with a printed paper dustjacket and plain boards is definitively a later printing regardless of its copyright-page statement; if the copyright page carries no printing statement, cross-check the jacket format before treating the copy as a first. Such copies are uncommon in the secondary market but not collectible as firsts; Lacey Books Ltd (Cirencester, UK) offered one example (AbeBooks UK listing 32333748497, inventory \# x3110254).

### 2.3 US pre-publication states — Uncorrected Proof and Advance Reader's Edition

Knopf issued **two distinct pre-publication softcover states** of *The Secret History*, separated by approximately 16 pages of uncorrected text and by completely different cover designs. They are catalogued separately as §2.3a (the Uncorrected Proof) and §2.3b (the Advance Reader's Edition).

**Page-count cascade across the four documented TSH text states (US Knopf):**

| State | Page count | Source of evidence |
|---|---|---|
| Knopf manuscript (typescript) | 866 pp | James Kaplan, "Smart Tartt," Vanity Fair Sept 1992 (§8.1) |
| **§2.3a Uncorrected Proof** (plain wraps) | **592 pp** | Back panel trade spec "Fiction, 5½ × 9¼, 592 pages, $23.00 FPT / 0-679-41032-5 / LC 92-53053" |
| **§2.3b Advance Reader's Edition** (glossy wraps) | 576 pp | an eBay listing |
| Trade first edition (Knopf hardcover) | 524 pp | §2.1 |

Three identifiable editing passes are documented between manuscript and publication: 866 → 592 (Knopf in-house cut), 592 → 576 (proof-to-ARE cut), 576 → 524 (ARE-to-print final cut). Tartt's statement to a correspondent — "I was rewriting all the way until press time" — is corroborated at the page-count level.

The Cochrane → Nietzsche/Plato epigraph swap (Cochrane's *Christianity and Classical Culture* in pre-pub states, replaced by Nietzsche's *Untimely Meditations* + Plato's *Republic* in the trade first) is documented in BOTH §2.3a and §2.3b as well as in the UK Viking proof (§2.5) — the proof epigraph state was shared across all three pre-pub copies before being changed for the published US and UK firsts alike.

---

#### 2.3a US Knopf Uncorrected Proof (plain wraps; 592 pp; the earlier pre-publication state)

**Covers:**
- **TSH-002a-1** — Full front wrap (entire cover, showing "THIS IS AN UNCORRECTED PROOF" upper box, title block, and "TENTATIVE PUBLICATION DATE / TENTATIVE PRICE / BOOK-OF-THE-MONTH CLUB / FIRST PRINTING 75,000 COPIES" lower box together): `assets/images/TSH-PROOF-US-1-frontcover_user.jpg` (315 KB)
- **TSH-002a-2** — Front wrap close-up detail of the lower box: `assets/images/TSH-PROOF-US-2-frontcover-detail_user.jpg` (385 KB)
- **TSH-002a-3** — Spine + 3/4 view (showing "Donna Tartt / THE SECRET HISTORY" spine lettering and Borzoi running-dog colophon): `assets/images/TSH-PROOF-US-3-spine-3qview_user.jpg` (282 KB)
- **TSH-002a-4** — Rear panel with publisher's blurb, B&W Tartt portrait, projected-jacket-art reduction, plot synopsis, and full trade spec including ISBN/LCCN/page count: `assets/images/TSH-PROOF-US-4-rearpanel_user.jpg` (342 KB)
- **TSH-002a-5** — Interior title page (minimalist geometric design "THE / SECRET / HISTORY / DONNA TARTT / ALFRED A. KNOPF NEW YORK 1992"): `assets/images/TSH-PROOF-US-5-titlepage_user.jpg` (195 KB)

Bibliographic block (from examined copy):

- Publisher: Alfred A. Knopf, Inc., New York; Borzoi imprint
- Pre-publication date statement: **"TENTATIVE PUBLICATION DATE: SEPTEMBER 1992"** (front wrap, lower box)
- Pre-publication price statement: **"TENTATIVE PRICE: $23"** (front wrap, lower box)
- Final-trade price on rear panel: **"$23.00 FPT"** — meaning Knopf had locked the trade price by the time the proof was printed but was still hedging on the front cover
- Print-run statement: **"FIRST PRINTING 75,000 COPIES"** printed on front wrap — Tier 1 primary-source confirmation of the 75,000 print run (consistent with Newsweek Sept 7 1992 and PW Sept 9 2002 secondary sources; documented in §2.1)
- Book-club statement: **"BOOK-OF-THE-MONTH CLUB and QUALITY PAPERBACK BOOK CLUB ALTERNATE SELECTIONS"** — primary-source confirmation of BOMC and QPB alternate selections (inferred in §2.2 from secondary sources)
- ISBN on rear panel: **0-679-41032-5** (same as the trade first — the proof was assigned the published ISBN at proof time)
- LCCN on rear panel: **92-53053** (same as the trade first)
- Pages: **592 pp** (rear panel trade spec)
- Trim size: **5½ × 9¼ inches** (rear panel trade spec)
- Wrappers: plain cream/uncoated stock; **black single-color typesetting only** — no jacket-art preview on the front; serif title block; thin black single-rule frame around upper and lower text boxes
- Front-wrap proof statement (upper box): **"THIS IS AN UNCORRECTED PROOF / It should not be quoted without comparison with the finished book"**
- Spine: cream stock with black lettering "Donna Tartt  THE SECRET HISTORY" reading head-to-foot; Borzoi running-dog colophon at foot
- Rear panel: Donna Tartt header; "THE SECRET HISTORY / A novel"; B&W author photograph (period portrait, c.1991–92); reduced reproduction of the projected jacket art (the atmospheric cloud/figure photograph that would become the printed acetate jacket); publisher's blurb ("A dazzling feat of psychological suspense—a big, richly textured, and hypnotic novel of golden youth corrupted by its own moral arrogance. A brilliant debut."); plot synopsis paragraph; bio line "**Donna Tartt lives in Mississippi and New York City.**" (note: NO Virginia reference at this date — the "Virginia-based" descriptor surfaces only in 2001 Artforum, §7.12); Borzoi colophon; trade-spec line
- Title page (interior): minimalist geometric design — stacked block-serif "THE / SECRET / HISTORY" with thin vertical rule between "THE" and the title block; "DONNA TARTT" in separate framed box below; "ALFRED A. KNOPF NEW YORK 1992" at foot

Identification points distinguishing the Uncorrected Proof from the Advance Reader's Edition (§2.3b):

1. **Wrappers are plain cream/uncoated stock** with black-only typesetting — NOT glossy and NOT in the white/grey/red/black palette of the ARE.
2. **No jacket-art preview on the front wrap.** The atmospheric photograph appears only as a small black-and-white reduction on the rear panel.
3. **"TENTATIVE" prefixed to publication date and price** on the front — the ARE drops "TENTATIVE" and prints the final date/price as firm.
4. **"BOOK-OF-THE-MONTH CLUB and QUALITY PAPERBACK BOOK CLUB ALTERNATE SELECTIONS"** notice printed on the front wrap — the ARE does not carry this notice on the front.
5. **"FIRST PRINTING 75,000 COPIES"** printed on the front wrap — the ARE does not carry this language on the front.
6. **Page count 592** vs. the ARE's 576 — a 16-page reduction between proof and ARE that documents one additional editing pass.
7. **Front-wrap proof statement: "THIS IS AN UNCORRECTED PROOF"** (the ARE carries the alternative language "Advance Reader's Edition" at the head plus "This is an Uncorrected Proof • Not For Sale" placement at base of rear panel).

Provenance / distribution: the Uncorrected Proof state was distributed to in-house Knopf readers and editors, the BOMC and QPB selection committees, and a small set of trade contacts well ahead of publication. The "TENTATIVE" prefix on date and price is diagnostic — by the time the polished ARE was prepared (with locked September 16, 1992 date and $23.00 price firm), Knopf's marketing department had moved on to broader reviewer distribution.

**WorldCat:** No WorldCat record (uncorrected proof; no separate OCLC assigned to proof state — the printed ISBN 0-679-41032-5 on the rear panel matches the trade first and so does not produce a discrete record).

The Uncorrected Proof is structurally scarcer than the ARE — it preceded the ARE in the production sequence and was distributed to a narrower audience (BOMC/QPB selectors, in-house readers) rather than the broader reviewer pool. Survival rate of plain-wraps proof copies is likely lower than glossy ARE copies because they were treated as working documents rather than promotional artefacts.

---

#### 2.3b US Knopf Advance Reader's Edition (glossy wraps; 576 pp; the later pre-publication state)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TSH-ARC-US-spine_ebay.jpg` — `TSH-002b` (US Knopf Advance Reader's Edition)

The authoritative collation, from Evening Star Books (ABAA / ILAB), is: glossy paperback, wrappers printed in white, grey, red, and black; **price of $23.00 firm on the rear wrapper** (NOT "TENTATIVE" — this is the key cover-state diagnostic vs. §2.3a); collation [18], 9–523, [7] pp. The base of the rear panel reads "This is an Uncorrected Proof • Not For Sale."

Distribution: the ARE state was the later, broader pre-publication distribution to reviewers and trade — produced after the §2.3a Uncorrected Proof, with the publication date and price now firm, the jacket art locked, and 16 pages of additional text trimmed (592 → 576). Both states share the Cochrane epigraph (subsequently swapped for Nietzsche/Plato in the trade first per the parent §2.3 note above).

Yesterday's Gallery (ABAA, East Woodstock CT) and Evening Star Books are reliable sources for the US ARE.

**WorldCat:** No WorldCat record (Advance Reader's Edition; no separate OCLC assigned).

**Physical data:** an eBay listing ("Vtg ADVANCED READERS EDITION The Secret History Donna Tartt Knopf 1992") documents the following physical measurements: **576 pages** (vs. 524 pages in the published trade first AND vs. 592 pages in the earlier §2.3a Uncorrected Proof); dimensions **9.5 × 5.9 × 1.8 inches**; weight **27.7 oz**. The 576-page count places this state midway between the Uncorrected Proof (§2.3a, 592 pp) and the trade first (§2.1, 524 pp).

**Saved Assets (§2.3b):**
- `assets/images/TSH-ARC-US-cover_ebay.jpg` — Cover of TSH US Advance Reader's Edition (Knopf 1992), showing glossy printed wrappers in white, grey, red, and black; sourced from an eBay listing. 295,499 bytes.
- `assets/images/TSH-ARC-US-spine_ebay.jpg` — Spine view of TSH US Advance Reader's Edition, confirming "ADVANCE READERS EDITION" lettering; sourced from an eBay listing. 380,537 bytes.

---

**Cross-reference for the dual-signed variant:** the Tartt-and-Bret-Easton-Ellis dual-signed advance copy offered via Barnebys (lot vqjmvlfwjj) is catalogued generically as a TSH ARC; the precise state (Uncorrected Proof §2.3a vs. Advance Reader's Edition §2.3b) has not been confirmed from photographic evidence. If the dual-signed copy is the §2.3a Uncorrected Proof, the association value is substantially higher because that state is the structurally scarcer of the two.

### 2.4 UK first edition (Viking, 1992)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TSH-UK-VIK92-signed-cover_ebay.jpg` — `TSH-003` (UK Viking 1st (Faun and Girl))


  - Publisher: Viking, London (Penguin Books)

  - Publication date: 1992

  - ISBN-10: 0-670-84854-9 / ISBN-13: 978-0-670-84854-6

  - Format: octavo, hardcover with dust jacket

UK firsts are scarce in like condition.

**WorldCat:** No separate OCLC confirmed via Open Library or WorldCat search; OL record OL18531069M (Viking 1992, 523pp, ISBN-10 0670848549).

### 2.5 UK Viking uncorrected proof (the proof epigraph variant)

**Cover:** *[cover image pending]* — `TSH-004` (UK Viking uncorrected proof (epigraph variant))


Stock \#43030 (now sold). Octavo, publisher's original paper wrappers, reproducing Clarence White's photograph "Faun and Girl." Per Jonkers's catalogue note:

  - The proof opens with a publisher's blurb that does not appear in the published edition.

  - Some details, including the price on the wrappers, were changed before publication.

  - Side-by-side textual comparison reveals the epigraphs were changed between proof and trade edition (see §2.3 — same Cochrane → Nietzsche/Plato swap as US Knopf advance state).

This is one of the most bibliographically significant pre-publication states in any Tartt book and is the textbook example of why proofs are collected: the proof is documentary evidence that a book existed in a different shape before publication.

**WorldCat:** No WorldCat record (uncorrected proof; no ISBN assigned to proof state).

### 2.5A UK Viking trade paperback trial binding (1992)

**Cover:** *[cover image pending]* — `TSH-005` (UK Viking trial binding 'snowfall')


  - Publisher: Viking, London (Penguin Books Ltd), 1992

  - Printing: second printing in paperback (number line with “1” removed; textual content is second printing)

  - Binding: publisher’s original illustrated paper wrappers reproducing Clarence White’s photograph “Faun and Girl” on a dark teal/blue-grey background. The distinguishing feature is a superimposed “snowfall effect”: a scattered pattern of large circular white dots (bubble-like, approximately 3–8mm diameter in proportion to the cover) overlaid across the front board, spine, and rear board. The overlay is dense and immediately conspicuous. The title page interior is plain cream stock: “DONNA TARTT / The SECRET HISTORY / VIKING” in an elegant serif typeface with no additional decoration.

  - Condition (Tom Wayling copy, SKU 1939): very good.

The “snowfall effect” wrappers were prepared by Viking for the first trade paperback printing of The Secret History but were deemed “an unsuccessful experiment” and withdrawn before that printing issued. A small number of second-printing copies were subsequently bound in the rejected trial-binding covers. Tom Wayling describes them as “reserved and issued on a small number of second printings.” The result is a genuine bibliographical curiosity: the covers are first-printing trial materials bound around second-printing text sheets. Very few copies are known to have reached the market.

Distinguishing features vs. standard UK Viking trade paperback: standard copies carry the “Faun and Girl” cover in clean photographic reproduction without any overlay. A trial-binding copy presents the same image with a conspicuous pattern of large white circular dots (the “snowfall effect”) across the entire exterior — front board, spine, and rear board. The dots are bubble-like rather than snow-like and are the probable reason the binding was rejected. There is no statement of “trial binding” on the book itself; the dot overlay is the sole physical identifier. First-printing copies have the same “Faun and Girl” cover WITHOUT this overlay.

**WorldCat:** No WorldCat record confirmed for this trial-binding variant state.

### 2.6 Penguin / Vintage paperback firsts

**Covers:**
- **TSH-006** — Penguin UK trade paperback 1st: *[cover image pending]*
- **TSH-007** — US Vintage Contemporaries paperback 1st: `assets/images/TSH-US-VINTAGE04-cover_publisher.jpg`


  - Penguin (UK) paperback first: ISBN 9780140167771 (1993)

  - Penguin reissue: ISBN 9780141035215 (2007); physical dimensions (an eBay listing): **18.1 × 11.1 × 5.28 cm; 0.32 kg; 640 pp**

  - Vintage Contemporaries (US) trade paperback first: ISBN 9781400031702 (April 13, 2004)

**WorldCat:** TSH UK Penguin paperback first (ISBN 9780140167771): [OCLC 52774181](https://www.worldcat.org/oclc/52774181) via Open Library OL18943981M (Penguin 1993, 629pp). TSH US Vintage Contemporaries first (ISBN 9781400031702): no separate OCLC confirmed via Open Library.

### 2.6A Ivy Books / Ballantine Books International Edition (May 1993)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TSH-IVY-INT-cover_abebooks.jpg` — `TSH-008` (Ivy Books International Edition)

**First International Ballantine Books Edition — May 1993**

  - **Imprint:** Ivy Books, Published by Ballantine Books, a division of Random House, Inc., New York
  - **Edition statement (copyright page):** "First International Ballantine Books Edition: May 1993"
  - **Published by arrangement with:** Alfred A. Knopf, Inc.
  - **Simultaneously published in Canada by:** Random House of Canada Limited, Toronto
  - **Format:** Mass market paperback
  - **ISBN-10:** 0-8041-1177-4
  - **ISBN-13:** 978-0-8041-1177-5
  - **Pages:** 512 (confirmed via AbeBooks ISBN record)
  - **Physical dimensions:** 6.8 × 4.2 × 1.1 in; approx. 8.7–9.1 oz (identical to companion domestic Ballantine edition OL7910485M)
  - **Library of Congress Catalog Card Number:** 92-52053
  - **Cover price:** $6.99 USD
  - **Cover label (front):** "IVY INTERNATIONAL EDITION/1177-4/$6.99"
  - **Manufactured in the United States of America; Cover printed in USA**
  - **Cover design:** Dark/atmospheric photographic cover with red title lettering; "THE HYPNOTIC BESTSELLER" banner at top; Ivy Books logo at foot of front cover
  - **Blurbs:** NYT Book Review ("A GRIPPING READ."), New York Times ("ENTHRALLING...A FEROCIOUSLY WELL-PACED ENTERTAINMENT."), Time ("A CHALLENGING COMBINATION OF A MYSTERY, AN EXPLORATION OF EVIL, BOTH BANAL AND BIZARRE, AND A GENEROUS SLICE OF THE WORLD AS SEEN BY THE AUTHOR.")

**Collector notes:** Ivy Books was Ballantine's international mass market paperback imprint, used for licensed reprints distributed internationally. This edition predates the more commonly cited US Vintage Contemporaries paperback (2004) by eleven years and uses a distinct cover design from both the Knopf hardcover and UK Penguin paperback. Condition varies significantly in the secondary market. Not a signed limited or collector edition but of bibliographic interest as the earliest US-published paperback reprint of TSH.

**Disambiguation note:** A separate edition listed elsewhere as "US Trade Paperback, Ballantine Books (1996), 978-0449911518" carries incorrect format, date, and ISBN attributions. The correct Ivy Books format is mass market paperback; the correct date is May 1993; the correct ISBN is 0-8041-1177-4 / 978-0-8041-1177-5. ISBN 9780449911518 does NOT correspond to the §2.6A/§2.6B 1993 Ballantine mass-market editions — it is a DISTINCT 1996 Random House/Ballantine trade paperback of TSH (592 pp, 8.2×5.5×1 in, 16.1 oz, LCCN 96-096755; Publisher: Random House Publishing Group; confirmed via an eBay listing, Minneapolis MN seller). That is a third US paperback of TSH predating the Vintage Contemporaries trade PB (2004) by 8 years; the seller mislabeled the listing "Advance Readers Edition" — it is a published trade paperback. It is catalogued separately at §2.6C.

**Online verification:**
- AbeBooks (https://www.abebooks.com/9780804111775/): Publisher confirmed as Ivy Books, 1993; 512 pages; softcover (scarce in market).
- Two distinct 1993 Ballantine mass market editions exist and must not be confused:
  1. **Domestic US edition** — Publisher: Ballantine Books; ISBN 9780804111355 (ISBN-10: 0804111359); Open Library OL7910485M; WorldCat: worldcat.org/isbn/9780804111355. This is the edition most commonly found in US used book market.
  2. **International Edition** — Imprint: Ivy Books; ISBN 9780804111775 (ISBN-10: 0804111774); "First International Ballantine Books Edition: May 1993"; no separate Open Library record identified. Significantly scarcer and higher-valued than the domestic counterpart.
- Open Library: The 52-edition list for work OL4321141W does not include a discrete record for ISBN 9780804111775; the closest record is OL7910485M (domestic Ballantine 9780804111355).
- WorldCat OCLC number for ISBN 9780804111775: not retrieved (WorldCat URL blocked; manual check recommended).

**Saved assets:**
- `assets/images/TSH-IVY-INT-cover_abebooks.jpg` — Cover image for ISBN 9780804111775 (Ivy Books International Edition), 306×500 px, sourced from AbeBooks ISBN record. Note: AbeBooks stock image; may be generic placeholder.
- `assets/images/TSH-BAL-DOM-cover_ebay.jpg` — Cover image for companion domestic edition ISBN 9780804111355 (Ballantine Books US edition, 1993), 291×500 px, sourced from eBay product listing. For comparison reference only.

### 2.6B Ballantine Books domestic US mass-market paperback (May 1993)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TSH-BAL-DOM93-cover_abebooks.jpg` — `TSH-009` (Ballantine US domestic mass-market 1993)


**First Ballantine Books Edition — May 1993 (domestic US)**

  - **Publisher:** Ballantine Books, a division of Random House, Inc., New York
  - **Edition statement (copyright page):** "First Ballantine Books Edition: May 1993"
  - **Published by arrangement with:** Alfred A. Knopf, Inc.
  - **Simultaneously published in Canada by:** Random House of Canada Limited, Toronto
  - **Format:** Mass market paperback
  - **ISBN-10:** 0804111359
  - **ISBN-13:** 978-0-8041-1135-5
  - **Pages:** 512
  - **Physical dimensions:** 6.8 × 4.2 × 1.1 in (mass market standard)
  - **Cover price:** $5.99 US / $6.99 Canada (printed on rear cover)

**Disambiguation from companion International Edition (§2.6A):**
Two distinct simultaneous 1993 Ballantine mass-market editions were released in May 1993. The domestic US edition (this entry, §2.6B) bears the imprint "Ballantine Books" and ISBN 9780804111355, while the International Edition (§2.6A) bears the imprint "Ivy Books" and ISBN 9780804111775. Both have 512 pages and identical physical dimensions. The domestic edition carries a lower US price point ($5.99 vs $6.99 for International) and was distributed through the standard US retail chain. The International Edition was intended for export markets and is significantly scarcer in the current US market. The two editions are sometimes conflated in bibliographic databases; they must be distinguished by ISBN and imprint on the copyright page.

**Open Library:** Record OL7910485M — Publisher: Ballantine Books; 512 pages; 1993. This OL record corresponds to the domestic edition (ISBN 9780804111355).

**WorldCat:** Confirmed via Open Library OL7910485M; OCLC search at https://www.worldcat.org/isbn/9780804111355.

**Collector significance:** The most commonly encountered TSH paperback in the US secondary market. Very common in used bookstores, charity shops, and online platforms. Not a high-demand collectible on its own; value is primarily as a reading copy or as a comparison piece alongside the scarcer Ivy Books International Edition (§2.6A). Tartt-signed copies of this paperback have not been documented in major dealer infrastructure.

**Online verification:**
- AbeBooks (https://www.abebooks.com/9780804111355/): Numerous used copies. Publisher listed as Ballantine Books; 1993; 512 pages; softcover.
- Open Library OL7910485M: Ballantine Books, 512pp, 1993 — confirmed entry for ISBN 9780804111355.
- Two distinct 1993 mass-market editions (§2.6A and §2.6B) confirmed as bibliographically separate through differing imprint lines and ISBNs.

**Saved assets:**
- `assets/images/TSH-BAL-DOM93-cover_abebooks.jpg` — Cover image for ISBN 9780804111355 (domestic Ballantine Books US Edition, 1993), sourced from AbeBooks ISBN record. 43,727 bytes; 200 OK. For comparison with §2.6A Ivy Books International Edition.

### 2.6C Random House trade paperback (1996)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TSH-US-RH96-cover_ebay.jpg` — `TSH-010` (Random House trade paperback 1996)


**1996 Random House / Ballantine trade paperback**

  - **Publisher:** Random House Publishing Group (Ballantine Books division)
  - **Year:** 1996
  - **Format:** Trade Paperback
  - **ISBN-10:** 0449911519
  - **ISBN-13:** 9780449911518
  - **Pages:** 592 (note: higher than the 512-page 1993 Ballantine mass-market PBs; different typesetting)
  - **Physical dimensions:** 8.2 × 5.5 × 1 in; 16.1 oz
  - **LCCN:** 96-096755
  - **Synopsis on rear panel:** "Selected by the Book-of-the-Month Club / A NEW YORK TIMES NOTABLE BOOK"

**Bibliographic context:** This is a distinct third US paperback edition of TSH, predating the Vintage Contemporaries trade paperback (2004) by 8 years. It is entirely separate from the 1993 Ballantine mass-market editions (§2.6A ISBN 9780804111775 / §2.6B ISBN 9780804111355). The 592-page count (vs. 512 pages in the 1993 Ballantine mass-market PBs) reflects re-typesetting for the trade paperback format. This edition has been incorrectly dismissed in some sources as a data error; an eBay listing (Minneapolis MN, Good condition) confirms it as a real published trade paperback, though the seller mislabeled it "Advance Readers Edition."

**Collector notes:** Not a collector priority on its own; primarily of bibliographic interest.

**Saved Assets (§2.6C):**
- `assets/images/TSH-US-RH96-cover_ebay.jpg` — Cover of 1996 Random House trade paperback of TSH (ISBN 9780449911518); sourced from an eBay listing. 242,097 bytes.

**WorldCat:** LCCN 96-096755 confirmed via eBay product listing data. WorldCat search at https://www.worldcat.org/isbn/9780449911518 recommended.

### 2.6D Penguin Red Classics Edition (2006)

**Cover:** `assets/images/_retrieved/TSH-RED-CLASSICS06-cover-amazon.jpg` — `TSH-014` (Penguin Red Classics 2006)

- **Publisher:** Penguin Books Ltd (UK)
- **Series:** Penguin Red Classics ("READ RED")
- **Year:** 2006
- **ISBN-10:** 0-14-102364-3
- **ISBN-13:** 978-0-14-102364-9
- **Format:** Paperback
- **Pages:** 658
- **Price:** £7.99
- **URL on spine/cover:** penguinclassics.com/reds

**Cover design (from eBay AU listing 278047548764):** Dark amber/sepia background with a large classical marble head filling the upper two-thirds of the cover — photographed from the Alinari Archives, Florence (credit confirmed from rear panel). Title "THE SECRET HISTORY" and author "DONNA TARTT" in gold/warm serif type below the face. Quote at top: *"Haunting, compelling and brilliant"* — THE TIMES. Small Penguin colophon top-right. Rear panel: "RED CLASSICS" header; "Sometimes evil is hard to recognize…" tagline; blurbs from *The New York Times* ("Enthralling…remarkably powerful"), Ruth Rendell ("It takes my breath away; it is so accomplished"), and John Grisham ("A beautifully written story…funny, sad, scary and impossible to leave alone"). "For classic fiction READ RED" sticker with Penguin logo. Cover design credit: **David Mann**. Cover image credit: **© Alinari Archives, Florence**.

**Publication context:** Penguin Red Classics was a UK imprint sub-brand launched c. 2006 — a line of literary fiction paperbacks in a bold, unified design aesthetic (dark covers, classical/archival imagery, sans-serif "RED CLASSICS" spine branding). The series used the penguinclassics.com/reds URL for promotion. TSH's assignment to this line — rather than Penguin's standard fiction list — reflects Penguin UK's decision to position the novel as a modern classic. The 658-page count is distinct from earlier Penguin UK typesettings (629pp in the 1993 first paperback; 630–640pp in the 2007 Celebrations edition), indicating a fresh typesetting for this edition.

**Collector notes:** Not signed or limited. The distinctive amber/classical-face cover makes this one of the more visually striking UK TSH paperbacks and is sometimes mistaken for an earlier or rarer edition due to the unfamiliar design. Moderately uncommon in the secondary market — not frequently listed, and its specific identity (Red Classics vs. standard Penguin) is often undescribed by sellers. The eBay AU listing (278047548764, condition Good) is the source copy for this entry's cover examination.

**Saved assets:**
- `assets/images/_retrieved/TSH-RED-CLASSICS06-cover-amazon.jpg` — Cover image, sourced from Amazon UK product page (ISBN 9780141023649). 521×800 px, 45,754 bytes.

**Canonical URLs:**
- Amazon UK: https://www.amazon.co.uk/dp/0141023643
- AbeBooks: https://www.abebooks.com/9780141023649/
- QBD Books (AU): https://www.qbd.com.au/penguin-red-classic-the-secret-history/donna-tartt/9780141023649/

### 2.6E Penguin Books (UK) Celebrations Edition (2007)

**Cover:** `assets/images/_retrieved/TSH-CELEBRATIONS07-cover-openlibrary.jpg` — `TSH-015` (Penguin UK Celebrations Edition 2007)

- **Publisher:** Penguin Books Ltd (UK)
- **Year:** 2007
- **Series:** Penguin Celebrations (Crime)
- **ISBN-10:** 0-14-103521-8
- **ISBN-13:** 978-0-14-103521-5
- **Format:** Paperback
- **Pages:** 630–640 (630 per Amazon; 640 per an eBay listing; minor discrepancy consistent with different typesetting counts)
- **Physical dimensions:** 5.16 × 1.1 × 7.72 in (Amazon); 18.1 × 11.1 × 5.28 cm, 0.32 kg (eBay)

**Cover design:** Iconic retro Penguin Crime design — vertical three-band layout (green top / cream white middle / green bottom). "PENGUIN BOOKS" in the classic diamond-shield logo at top of green section. Author name "Donna Tartt" and title "The Secret History" in black serif type on the cream middle band. "CRIME" printed vertically in small caps on both left and right edges of the cover. Penguin colophon (standing penguin) in white at foot of lower green section. The design deliberately mimics Penguin's original 1930s–1950s Crime series aesthetic.

**Publication context:** The Penguin Celebrations series was a 2007 UK initiative issuing classic Penguin titles in replica vintage-format covers, organised by the original Penguin genre colour-coding (green = Crime, orange = Fiction, blue = Non-Fiction, etc.). TSH was designated as "Crime" in the Penguin catalogue — consistent with its treatment across Penguin's UK paperback history — and issued in the green Crime livery. The series was marketed as a collectible brand celebrating Penguin's design heritage; individual titles were not limited or numbered.

**Relation to §2.6:** This edition is the same Penguin Books Ltd (UK) publisher but is a distinct imprint sub-brand from the 1993 Penguin UK paperback first (ISBN 9780140167771, §2.6/TSH-006). It is already noted in §2.6 as "Penguin reissue: ISBN 9780141035215 (2007)" with physical dimensions — this entry expands that note into a full bibliographic record.

**Collector notes:** Not a signed or numbered limited edition. Moderately scarce in the current secondary market. The distinctive retro cover design makes it visually the most striking of the UK Penguin TSH paperback editions. Low collector premium unless signed; primary interest is as a design-history artefact of the Penguin Celebrations brand.

**Saved assets:**
- `assets/images/_retrieved/TSH-CELEBRATIONS07-cover-openlibrary.jpg` — Cover image for ISBN 9780141035215, sourced from Open Library cover API. 329×500 px, 37,501 bytes; 200 OK.

**Canonical URLs:**
- AbeBooks: https://www.abebooks.com/9780141035215/
- Amazon UK: https://www.amazon.co.uk/dp/0141035218
- Open Library cover: https://covers.openlibrary.org/b/isbn/9780141035215-L.jpg

### 2.7 Bloomsbury 2009 boxed signed limited (TSH + TLF)

**Cover:** `assets/images/rId70.jpg` — `TSH-011` (Bloomsbury 2009 boxed signed limited (TSH+TLF))


![Fig. 2.7 — Bloomsbury 2009 signed boxed set (TSH + TLF), copy \#844/1000. Full clamshell case with silver Bloomsbury logo. Photo: Leland Little Auctions, Lot 6031.](assets/images/rId70.jpg "Fig. 2.7 — Bloomsbury 2009 signed boxed set (TSH + TLF), copy #844/1000. Full clamshell case with silver Bloomsbury logo. Photo: Leland Little Auctions, Lot 6031.")

Fig. 2.7 — Bloomsbury 2009 signed boxed set (TSH + TLF), copy \#844/1000. Full clamshell case with silver Bloomsbury logo. Photo: Leland Little Auctions, Lot 6031.

  - Title: The Secret History & The Little Friend — Signed Limited Edition Box Set
  - Publisher: Bloomsbury Publishing PLC (London)
  - Date: November 2, 2009
  - Limitation: 1000 numbered sets
  - ISBN: 9781408802922
  - Format: 2 hardcover volumes in slipcase. The volumes have decorated paper boards (NOT cloth — note: some dealer descriptions say “black cloth” but that refers to the SLIPCASE, the volumes themselves are decorated paper boards). Page edges silver-gilt. Ribbon bookmarks. Wood-free, acid-free paper. Specially designed endpapers. Slipcase is black cloth. Pagination: [viii], 628, [4]pp. (TSH vol.); [x], 555, [11]pp. (TLF vol.).
  - Slipcase dimensions: \~9.5" × 6.5" × 4.5"
  - Signing: BOTH volumes signed by Tartt on the limitation page in VENETIAN ink (corroborated across multiple dealer descriptions and Bloomsbury announcement)
  - Provenance line: limitation page text typically reads to the effect of “This is one of one thousand sets…”

Auction record: - Leland Little Auctions Lot 6031, Sept 17 2025 (Auction 232155 — Collectible Books, Maps & Documents) — set \#844/1000 from the Bruce R. Kuniholm Collection (University Distinguished Service Professor at Duke). Most-significant institutional-provenance Bloomsbury 2009 set in the open auction record. - Bloomsbury Auctions Jun 8 2012 — Deluxe Limited \#x/350 in mixed lot for $340 (note: this appears to refer to the TLF 350-copy Deluxe Limited per §3.4, NOT the 1000-copy TSH+TLF box set; cross-check needed)

Retail / distribution channel: confirmed as a Waterstones exclusive (UK), listed with publisher attribution "Viking / Waterstones" — the edition was sold directly through Waterstones stores and online.

Forgery red flags: - Number outside 1-1000 range - Non-Venetian ink at limitation page - Missing slipcase - Volumes presented as cloth (the volumes are decorated paper boards; the slipcase is black cloth) - Single volume sold as “Bloomsbury 2009 limited” — the set was issued only as a 2-volume slipcased set; single volumes circulating separately have been broken from sets and are bibliographically inferior

  - ISBN-13: 9781408802922

  - Limitation: 1,000 signed and numbered copies

  - Binding: black paper-covered boards, blind-stamped decoration, silver lettering on spines, all edges silver, black ribbon bookmark in each

  - Both volumes signed by Tartt in Venetian ink (program-specific colour — see §9)

  - Printed on wood-free, acid-free paper; specially designed endpapers

  - Volume size: 9.5 × 6.5 inches; each volume in dust jacket; matching slipcase

**WorldCat:** No OCLC confirmed via Open Library search for ISBN 9781408802922. OL record OL42870465M exists; OL date "Nov 19, 2013" is a data error — actual pub date November 2, 2009 per dealer and auction records.

### 2.7A Penguin Books (UK) 25th Anniversary Paperback Edition (2017)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TSH-UK-25ANN-cover_abebooks.jpg` — `TSH-012` (Penguin UK 25th Anniversary 2017)


**25th Anniversary Edition — August 3, 2017 (UK)**

  - **Publisher:** Penguin Books Ltd (Penguin / Viking imprint), London
  - **Edition statement:** 25th Anniversary Edition
  - **Format:** Trade paperback / softcover
  - **ISBN-10:** 024198288X
  - **ISBN-13:** 978-0-241-98288-4
  - **Published:** August 3, 2017
  - **Pages:** 629
  - **Cover design:** New anniversary cover treatment; Penguin Books imprint on spine

**Publication context:** Penguin Books (UK) issued this paperback to mark the 25th anniversary of The Secret History (first published by Alfred A. Knopf and Viking in September 1992). The 629-page count matches the standard Penguin UK typesetting used for TSH (consistent with the 1993 Penguin PB first, ISBN 9780140167771 per §2.6). Issued as a standard trade paperback for the general market, not a signed or numbered limited edition.

**Distinction from signed limited §2.8:** The Viking 30th Anniversary (§2.8, ISBN 9780241621912, 2022) is a signed numbered limited of 500 copies in cloth binding. This 25th Anniversary (§2.7A) is a standard unsigned trade paperback and is far more common in the market.

**Open Library:** No discrete Open Library record confirmed for ISBN 9780241982884; may be catalogued under a broader Penguin record.

**WorldCat:** Not confirmed via Open Library; WorldCat search at https://www.worldcat.org/isbn/9780241982884 recommended for OCLC number.

**Collector significance:** A secondary collecting priority. Desirable as part of a complete format run and for its anniversary cover design, but not scarce. Tartt-signed copies of this edition have not been documented in major dealer infrastructure.

**Online verification:**
- AbeBooks (https://www.abebooks.com/9780241982884/): Listed as "Penguin Books Ltd, 2017; 629pp; softcover."
- ISBN 9780241982884 confirmed via AbeBooks ISBN record: Publisher Penguin Books Ltd; August 3, 2017; 629 pages.

**Saved assets:**

| PL / Polish (reissue) | Tajemna Historia | Znak Literanova (Kraków) | 2022 | Jerzy Kozłowski | 9788324077434 | 2022 reissue with new translation by Kozłowski; original 1995 Zysk i S-ka (Paweł Witkowski) is the first |
| KO / Korean (reissue) | 비밀의 계절 | 은행나무 (EunHaeng Namu) | 2015 | Unverified | 9788956608556 | 2015 revised edition; original 1992 까치글방 (Kachi Gul Bang) is the first |

Notes on chronology: Korea (1992), the same year as publication, is the earliest non-English first traced. Japan (1994) and Italy (1992/93), France/Germany/Netherlands/Poland (1993–95) cluster in the immediate post-publication years. Russia is unusual — the first Russian translation did not appear until 2009, 17 years after the original publication, reflecting both copyright realities of the 1990s post-Soviet market and a delayed wave of literary translation that picked up around the late 2000s. The Russian Inostranka 2009 first is therefore both scarce and historically interesting.

The Japanese case is also unusual: the original 1994 Fusosha edition (under the literal title シークレット・ヒストリー) was reissued by Shinchosha at a later date under the retitled 黙約 (Mokuyaku, "Silent Pact"), with an afterword by Haruki Murakami. For collectors, the original Fusosha two-volume set is the bibliographic first; the Shinchosha retitled edition has its own appeal as a Murakami-introduced edition.

### 2.10 Audiobook editions of The Secret History

**Covers:**
- **TSH-014** — TSH 2023 Unabridged Audiobook (Tartt narrated): `assets/images/rId22.jpg` *(shares cover with print edition)*
- **TSH-015** — TSH unabridged audiobook (Karen White, Penguin Audio): `assets/images/rId22.jpg` *(shares cover with print edition)*


TSH 2023 Unabridged Audiobook narrated by DONNA TARTT

  - Publisher: Random House Audio
  - Release date: July 11, 2023 [2]
  - Format: digital audiobook (Audible / Amazon / Apple Books / Audible.com)
  - ASIN: B0C6FJPXNN (US) / B0C6FKCXMX (Canada)
  - Narrator: Donna Tartt (the first complete Tartt-narrated unabridged recording of TSH; 1993 cassette extracts were Tartt-narrated but only as extracts)
  - Significance: Tartt has narrated the audiobooks of (1) TLF abridged 2002, (2) True Grit 2006, and (3) participated in Winesburg Ohio multi-voice. The TSH 2023 unabridged is her first complete recording of her own debut novel — 31 years after publication.

Prior to the 2023 unabridged recording, Tartt did not narrate any commercially issued recording of The Secret History. The only earlier Tartt-narrated audiobook of her own fiction in the public record is the abridged The Little Friend (Random House Audio, 2002; see §3.7).

### 2.15 Easton Press signed leather edition of The Secret History

**Cover:** `assets/images/rId72.jpg` — `TSH-016` (Easton Press signed leather edition)


![Fig. 2.15 — Easton Press signed leather edition of The Secret History (2014), sealed in original collector's box. Full leather binding. Photo: AbeBooks dealer listing.](assets/images/rId72.jpg "Fig. 2.15 — Easton Press signed leather edition of The Secret History (2014), sealed in original collector's box. Full leather binding. Photo: AbeBooks dealer listing.")

Fig. 2.15 — Easton Press signed leather edition of The Secret History (2014), sealed in original collector's box. Full leather binding. Photo: AbeBooks dealer listing.

Per J. Levine Auction Apr 28, 2016 lot data: Easton Press, the signed-leather-binding modern-classics publisher, issued a signed leather edition of The Secret History.

Bibliographic block:

  - Title: The Secret History (Easton Press signed edition)
  - Publisher: Easton Press, Norwalk CT
  - Date: 2014 (multiple active AbeBooks dealer listings confirm 2014 as publication year; described as 1st Edition, Limited Edition)
  - Format: full leather binding (burgundy/dark red — confirmed from product photographs); 22kt gold accents; gold Greek key border on boards; classical profile medallion on front board; silk moire endpapers; ribbon marker; issued with original Easton Press presentation box; copies typically sold Mint/Sealed in original shrink wrap. ISBN not recorded.
  - Signature: signed by Tartt at the limitation page
  - Distribution: Easton Press direct subscription only (not sold through bookstores)

Auction record: 5-piece Easton Press signed lot (Edward P. Jones “The Known World” + Donna Tartt “The Secret History” + Buzz Aldrin “Magnificent Desolation” + Charlaine Harris “Dead Until Dark” + James D. Watson “The Double Helix”) sold at J. Levine Auction Apr 28, 2016, Arizona US, for USD $375 (estimate $300, 25% above estimate). Lot description: “All the books in this lot are sealed in the original cellophane and signed edition modern classics.” [3]

Collector authentication notes:

  - Easton Press signed-leather editions ship in cellophane wrap and remain sealed for their lifecycle if not opened — collectors should look for sealed copies as the highest-tier collectible state
  - Limitation page is signed (not bookplate)
  - Easton Press leather binding has gold-stamped spine and decorations
  - Authenticity of an Easton Press TSH should be verified against Easton Press’s own subscriber records — direct query to Easton Press recommended

**WorldCat:** No ISBN documented; WorldCat lookup not attempted without confirmed ISBN.

### 2.13 Large-print editions

TSH large-print edition: not located in dealer infrastructure. If a large-print TSH was issued by Random House Large Print, Center Point, Thorndike, or Wheeler, it has not been catalogued by ABAA dealers, AbeBooks, or accessible library finding aids. (TLF and TG large-print editions are documented separately; see §3.8 and §4.15.)

### 2.14 E-book editions

TSH e-book: digital editions are available via Amazon Kindle, Apple Books, Google Play Books, and Kobo. Kindle ASINs vary by territory. Knopf converted the 1992 backlist title to digital format at some point after the Kindle Store launched in November 2007. The Kindle first-issuance ASIN is B005PRJT9Q (Vintage Contemporaries edition), pub. Knopf Doubleday Publishing Group / Random House LLC, release date October 19, 2011.
## 3. The Little Friend (2002)

### 3.1 US first edition (Alfred A. Knopf, New York)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TLF-US-K1_1_c1801f234a.jpg` — `TLF-001` (US Knopf 1st/1st (orange/red jacket))


![Figure 3.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st of The Little Friend, jacket design by Chip Kidd, $26.00 jacket price. Photo: Evening Star Books (ABAA / ILAB, T2)](assets/images/rId31.jpg "Figure 3.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st of The Little Friend, jacket design by Chip Kidd, $26.00 jacket price. Photo: Evening Star Books (ABAA / ILAB, T2)")

Figure 3.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st of The Little Friend, jacket design by Chip Kidd, $26.00 jacket price. Photo: Evening Star Books (ABAA / ILAB, T2)

*Figure 3.1 — US Knopf 1st/1st of The Little Friend, jacket design by Chip Kidd, $26.00 jacket price. Photo: Evening Star Books (ABAA / ILAB, T2)*

  - Publisher: Alfred A. Knopf, New York

  - Publication date: October 22, 2002

  - ISBN-10: 0-679-43938-2

  - OCLC: 49603052; LC class PS3570.A657 L58 2002; Dewey 813/.54

  - Pages: collation [16], 3–555, [7] pp.; 555 numbered pages; 576 pp. counted including all leaves

  - Format: octavo

  - Binding: black paper boards with silver lettering on the front board and spine; black endpapers and pastedowns

  - Dust jacket: $26.00 price on front flap; jacket design by Chip Kidd

  - Illustrated title page

Identification points

11. "First edition" / first printing copyright-page statement

12. Black paper boards (NOT cloth) with silver lettering on front and spine

13. Black endpapers and pastedowns

14. Jacket design by Chip Kidd; $26.00 jacket price

15. Octavo, 555 numbered pages

16. Collector variant -- copies signed by Tartt and jacket designer Chip Kidd. First-edition copies of TLF inscribed by Donna Tartt and signed by jacket designer Chip Kidd have appeared at Raptis Rare Books. One example (item 140777) is a presentation copy inscribed on the half-title ("Merry Christmas Mark\! from Donna") plus signed three times by Chip Kidd on the title page, front jacket panel, and rear jacket flap; Fine in a near fine dust jacket. Jacket credited to Chip Kidd alone (unlike TSH which credits Kidd and Barbara de Wilde jointly).

**WorldCat:** [OCLC 49603052](https://www.worldcat.org/oclc/49603052) (Open Library OL3567617M).
**ISBN-13:** 9780679439387 (Open Library OL3567617M).
**LCCN:** 2002066878 (Open Library OL3567617M).

### 3.2 US uncorrected proof / advance reading copy

**Cover:** `assets/images/TLF-US-ARC-cover.jpg` — `TLF-002` (US Knopf uncorrected proof / ARC)


  - Publisher: Alfred A. Knopf, 2002

  - Format: softcover; original beige printed card wrappers (note: NOT glossy)

  - Dimensions: octavo (23.25cm)

  - Collation: [xvi], [2], 3–555, [5] pp.

  - Lorne Bair description: "The proof state is elusive, preceding the more common glossy advance copies." This wording indicates TLF may have had two distinct pre-publication states (the elusive beige-card-wrappers proof, then a more common glossy advance).

Wrapper text, verbatim:

  - Front cover: "THE LITTLE FRIEND / A Novel / Donna Tartt" (black serif type on beige/cream card stock)
  - Spine: "Donna Tartt / THE LITTLE FRIEND / Knopf"
  - Rear wrapper carries publisher boilerplate including: "Publication date: 1 November 2002" (NB: the actual US publication date was October 22, 2002 — this proof predates retail by approximately 10 days); Price: $26.00; First printing: 300,000 copies; note of simultaneous Random House Audio availability.

This confirms: (a) proof wrappers are plain beige card (not glossy), (b) the printing quantity of 300,000 copies for first printing, (c) the proof was prepared before the retail date was finalised.

The beige uncorrected proof is the earlier and scarcer of the two pre-publication states.

**WorldCat:** No WorldCat record (advance reading copy; no ISBN assigned to beige-wrapper proof state).

### 3.2A TLF per-printing matrix (US Knopf)

Parallel to the TSH matrix in §2.2. Multiple later printings exist; the dealer record confirms 1st through 4th printings actively traded among ABAA dealers.

| | | |
| ---------------------- | ---------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Printing** | **Copyright-page statement** | **Notes** |
| 1st printing | "First edition" stated, no other printing line | Pub date 10/22/2002; the trade collectible state. Black paper boards, silver lettering, $26 jacket |
| 2nd printing | "Second printing" stated | Standard in-month or near-publication reprint |
| 3rd printing | "Third printing" stated | — |
| 4th printing | "Fourth printing" stated | Confirmed via signed-by-author 4th-printing dealer listing |
| 5th printing and later | Each carries explicit printing statement | Per-printing dealer cataloguing thins beyond 4th |

Compared with The Secret History (which had a notable "Second Printing Before Publication" state), TLF does NOT appear to have had a pre-publication second printing. The pre-publication anticipated demand was less aggressive for TLF than for the 1992 TSH.

### 3.3 UK first edition trade hardcover (Bloomsbury, 2002)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TLF-RBC_8fb3f21e4b.jpg` — `TLF-003` (UK Bloomsbury trade hardcover 1st)


3.3.1 Publishing context: Alexandra Pringle and the Bloomsbury 2002 calendar

Alexandra Pringle has been Bloomsbury Publishing’s group editor-in-chief since 2000 and was Tartt's UK editor for The Little Friend. Pringle acquired TLF in a competitive London auction; multiple UK publishers bid for the manuscript and Bloomsbury's winning advance was reported at “almost £1m” in the Bookseller and Irish Times trade-press coverage [8]. Pringle is one of the most consequential UK literary editors of her generation; her Bloomsbury fiction list includes Khaled Hosseini, William Boyd, Margaret Atwood, Esi Edugyan, and Anne Enright among others. Her acquisition of TLF was a flagship Bloomsbury move; the embargo programme described in §8.2 reflects the magnitude of Bloomsbury's commercial expectations.

The 2002 Bloomsbury / Harry Potter calendar context: Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire was published in July 2000; Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix did not appear until June 21, 2003 [9]. 2002 was therefore a “fallow” Harry Potter year for Bloomsbury — the publisher needed a flagship literary title to anchor its 2002 list. The Little Friend was that title. The £1m advance, the October 28, 2002 UK launch (six days after the US Knopf publication of October 22, 2002), the Deluxe quarter-leather Limited Edition (350 copies), and the strict pre-publication embargo programme (Bookseller, September 2002) collectively reflect Bloomsbury's investment in TLF as the year's major Bloomsbury fiction event in the absence of a new Harry Potter release. This context is relevant to collectors because the Deluxe Limited Edition's 350-copy limitation, the Bloomsbury promotional intensity, and the institutional investment that produced the now-historical embargo memo all trace to the same publishing-calendar logic.

UK trade hardcover. Jacket design (UK) credited to Chip Kidd in some references; the UK jacket may differ from the US jacket. UK firsts are common at modest prices.

**WorldCat:** No separate OCLC for ISBN 9780747562115 (UK Bloomsbury 2002). Master work OCLC 49603052 covers US Knopf; UK Bloomsbury catalogued under same work record. Correct ISBN-13 for UK edition: 9780747562115 (not 9780747562113).

### 3.4 UK Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited Edition (2002)

**Cover:** `assets/images/rId34.jpg` — `TLF-004` (UK Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited 350 signed)


![Figure 3.4 — UK Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited Edition of The Little Friend (2002), one of 350 signed and numbered copies. Quarter-bound: bright orange paper boards, blind-stamped, with black leather spine in copper-orange titling, in a black cloth-covered slipcase. Photo: Sue Lloyd-Davies Books / Biblio (T2)](assets/images/rId34.jpg "Figure 3.4 — UK Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited Edition of The Little Friend (2002), one of 350 signed and numbered copies. Quarter-bound: bright orange paper boards, blind-stamped, with black leather spine in copper-orange titling, in a black cloth-covered slipcase. Photo: Sue Lloyd-Davies Books / Biblio (T2)")

Figure 3.4 — UK Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited Edition of The Little Friend (2002), one of 350 signed and numbered copies. Quarter-bound: bright orange paper boards, blind-stamped, with black leather spine in copper-orange titling, in a black cloth-covered slipcase. Photo: Sue Lloyd-Davies Books / Biblio (T2)

*Figure 3.4 — UK Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited Edition of The Little Friend (2002), one of 350 signed and numbered copies. Quarter-bound: bright orange paper boards, blind-stamped, with black leather spine in copper-orange titling, in a black cloth-covered slipcase. Photo: Sue Lloyd-Davies Books / Biblio (T2)*

  - Publisher: Bloomsbury, London (October 2002)

  - ISBN-13: 9780747564225

  - Limitation: 350 signed and numbered copies

  - Binding: quarter-bound with rexine-backed boards (bright orange paper boards blind-stamped with decoration, black leather spine in copper-orange titling); Christie's lot 224 Jun 2022 uses the term "rexine-backed boards"

  - Endpapers: orange; page fore-edges in orange

  - Bookmark: integral copper-coloured silk

  - Slipcase: black cloth-covered slipcase

  - Signed by Tartt under printed name on title page; numbered at foot of same page

Auction records: Forum Auctions Lot 224, Jun 9 2022 — Deluxe Limited \#x/350 in bundled lot of c.110 twentieth-century literature — unsold. Bloomsbury Auctions Jun 8 2012 — Deluxe Limited \#x/350 in mixed lot incl. Setterfield + White + Higgins + Unsworth — sold $340. Forum / Bloomsbury Auctions Mar 6 2013 — TLF Deluxe Limited \#x/350 in 9-vol signed limiteds lot — sold $1,182 (290% above $303 estimate).

Forgery red flags: number outside 1-350 range; non-quarter-leather binding state; missing slipcase; limitation page absent or modified.

**WorldCat:** No OCLC confirmed via Open Library for ISBN 9780747564225.

### 3.5 UK Bloomsbury Advance Review Copy, signed

**Cover:** `assets/images/rId73.jpg` — `TLF-005` (UK Bloomsbury Advance Review Copy (940 signed))


![Fig. 3.5 — UK Bloomsbury advance review copy of The Little Friend (2002), one of 940 signed copies. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (RRB-140777).](assets/images/rId73.jpg "Fig. 3.5 — UK Bloomsbury advance review copy of The Little Friend (2002), one of 940 signed copies. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (RRB-140777).")

Fig. 3.5 — UK Bloomsbury advance review copy of The Little Friend (2002), one of 940 signed copies. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (RRB-140777).

Bibliographic block:

  - Title: The Little Friend (Advance Review Copy)
  - Publisher: Bloomsbury Publishing Ltd, London
  - Date: 2002 (pre-publication; preceded the October 28, 2002 trade hardcover by approximately 2-3 months based on UK trade-distribution patterns)
  - Format: softcover wraps, w/o dust jacket
  - Pagination: 545 pp
  - Trim size: 16 cm × 12 cm (substantially smaller than the trade hardcover, consistent with UK ARC trade-distribution format)
  - Limitation: 940 copies (numbered)
  - Signature: signed by Donna Tartt on title page (in Tartt's standard ink across this signing programme)
  - Identification points: limitation statement; signature on title page; soft wraps without DJ; 16 cm × 12 cm trim is the diagnostic identifier.

Significance: this is the UK promotional signed proof state of TLF. The 940-copy signed ARC is bibliographically distinct from:

  - The Bloomsbury trade hardcover first edition (October 28, 2002, £16.99, ISBN 0747562113) — §3.3
  - The Bloomsbury Deluxe Limited Edition (350 copies, quarter-leather, signed and numbered) — §3.4

The 940-copy signed ARC therefore sits between the trade first and the Deluxe Limited as the third documented signed UK Tartt-launch state. Distribution was to UK trade reviewers and select retailers in the run-up to the October 28, 2002 launch — consistent with the strict embargo programme documented in §8.2.

Auction record: Catawiki realized USD $1,786 on September 23, 2016 (NL sale) for copy \#130 of 940. This is one of the higher-realised TLF auction prices on record and reflects the rarity of the signed pre-publication state. Known 940-copy ARCs appear to be largely in private hands or to have moved through European auction channels rather than US ABAA dealers.

Collector authentication notes:

  - Limitation page should number the copy out of 940
  - Signature on title page (not bookplate)
  - Soft wraps (no DJ as issued)
  - Period-correct ink (consistent with Tartt 2002 signing programme — standard brown/blue ink)
  - 16 × 12 cm is the canonical trim; if a copy presents as Deluxe Limited dimensions, suspect mis-cataloguing

**WorldCat:** No WorldCat record (advance review copy; no separate ISBN confirmed for this ARC state).

Eleven foreign firsts have credentialed first-edition records. The Dutch first is the chronological true first — a publishing pattern De Bezige Bij would repeat with Het puttertje a decade later.
