| Kate Bernheimer | Editor's Note |

**Collecting significance:**
- **First documented Tartt translation.** No prior reference in this catalogue, in ISFDB, in Wikipedia, or in the Donna Tartt Shrine notes a Tartt-as-translator credit.
- *Les Illuminations* is Rimbaud's late prose-poem cycle (composed c. 1872–1875, published posthumously 1886 in *La Vogue*). Tartt's selection of Rimbaud is consistent with her literary affinities (cf. the Bookforum/Slate Pietsch conversation 2013, where she discusses French and Russian 19th-century writers as foundational).
- Tartt's two contributions to *Fairy Tale Review* — the 2005 essay "From Barrie to Stevenson" (§7.19, Blue Issue) and the 2006 Rimbaud translations (this entry, Green Issue) — constitute a two-issue Kate Bernheimer / Fairy Tale Review programme spanning 2005–2006, the same period of her True Grit introduction (§7.1, 2005).

**Canonical URL:** Wayne State University Press product page: https://shop.prod.wayne.edu/wsupjournals/wsupjournals/fairy-tale-review/fairy-tale-review-back-issues/the-green-issue.html

Full text extracted from `assets/sources/archive/FairyTaleReview-Vol2-GreenIssue-2006-9780814341711-AnnasArchive.epub`.

**The four Rimbaud poems Tartt translated:**

1. **"Bottom"** — French original ("La réalité étant trop épineuse pour mon grand caractère...") + Tartt's English translation ("Reality being entirely too spiny and thorny for my grand character...").
2. **"Being Beauteous"** ("Devant une neige un Etre de Beauté de haute taille...") + Tartt's translation ("An Ideal of Beauty, standing tall before snow...").
3. **"Vies"** ("Lives") — three numbered sections (I, II, III). Section I begins "O les énormes avenues du pays saint..." / "O the enormous avenues of the Holy land...". Section III closes "Je suis réellement d'outre-tombe, et pas de commissions." / "I really am from beyond the grave, and without obligations."
4. **"Phrases"** — multiple aphoristic prose-poem fragments. Begins "Quand le monde sera réduit en un seul bois noir pour nos quatre yeux étonnés..." / "Some day, when the world boils down to a single black wood for our four astonished eyes..."

**Source-text edition:** Rimbaud's *Les Illuminations* (composed c. 1872–1875; first published posthumously 1886 in *La Vogue*). Tartt presents her translations en face — French original on one page, English translation on the facing page.

**Editorial framing (Carmen Giminez Smith, Green Issue editor's note on Rimbaud):** Brief biographical note on Rimbaud ("born in 1854, in a small town called Charleville in the Ardennes... began writing poetry at age thirteen... by age 19 had completed *The Drunken Boat*, *A Season in Hell* and *The Illuminations*... gave up writing forever; he went to Africa, where he worked at exporting coffee and running guns; and was dead by the age of 37"). Quotes Rimbaud from *Une Saison en Enfer: Délires II* on his love of "dumb paintings, scenes painted in door panels, stage sets, painted canvas backdrops for acrobats, flags and standards, popular colored prints, old novels gone out of fashion, church Latin, erotic books with bad spelling, the novels of our grandmothers, fairy tales, little books from childhood, foolish refrains and naive rhythms."

**Author bio (in contributor notes):** "DONNA TARTT is the author of the novels *The Secret History* and *The Little Friend*." (Same as Blue Issue 2005 — confirms pre-Goldfinch context.)

The selection (Bottom, Being Beauteous, Vies, Phrases) draws from across *Les Illuminations* and is consistent with Tartt's documented French-language reading (cf. her Camus dinner-date answer in §7.16; her time in France carrying *The Unquiet Grave* by Cyril Connolly). This is the first and only documented Tartt translation programme of any text by another author.

### 7.23 Foreword by Donna Tartt — *The Life of St. Francis* by St. Bonaventure (HarperCollins Spiritual Classics, February 1, 2005)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TARTT-FOREWORD-LifeStFrancis-HarperOne-2005_cover_openlibrary.jpg` — front cover prominently shows "Foreword by Donna Tartt" beneath the title.

**Bibliographic record:**

| Field | Data |
|---|---|
| Title | *The Life of St. Francis: A Classic Biography and Inspiring Spiritual Treatise on Gospel Perfection* |
| Source author | **Bonaventure** (c. 1221–1274), Saint and Cardinal — Tuscan scholastic theologian and Franciscan mystic; composed this official biography of St. Francis of Assisi in 1260 (commissioned by the Franciscan Order in 1250 per the cover blurb; composition completed 1260–1263 per scholarship) |
| Translator | **Ewert Cousins** |
| Foreword | **Donna Tartt** |
| Series | HarperCollins Spiritual Classics |
| Series editor | Emilie Griffin (per excerpted text) |
| Publisher (1st printing) | Harper San Francisco |
| Publisher (later printings) | HarperOne / HarperCollins |
| Publication date | February 1, 2005 (1st printing per Open Library); September 1, 2009 (later reprint per Barnes & Noble) |
| ISBN-13 | 978-0-06-057652-3 |
| ISBN-10 | 0-06-057652-9 |
| Format | Paperback, 176 pp |
| Dimensions | 5.31 × 8.00 × 0.40 in. |

**Tartt's contribution:** A ~1,100-word foreword running **pp. v–ix** (Roman-numeral front-matter pagination, 5 pp.), signed "Donna Tartt" at the end. Copyright statement: **"Foreword © 2005 by Donna Tartt. All rights reserved."** Header: "FOREWORD" (no separate Tartt-given title). The foreword has three distinct parts:

1. **Theological/literary framing of Francis** (pp. v–vi). Tartt sets up Francis as "the greatest ambassador of the Church—the ideal introduction to Christianity for people of different faiths and cultures." She characterizes his message as "a faith so radiantly inclusive that it hails the birds as sisters, and addresses a cricket with as much reverence and courtesy as a bishop." Cites G.K. Chesterton on Francis "[anticipating] all that is most liberal and sympathetic in the modern mood; the love of nature; the love of animals, the sense of social compassion..."
2. **Bonaventure's craft** (p. vii). Tartt explains why Bonaventure (canonized only two years after Francis's death) wrote this life: "Bonaventure's anecdotes give a sharp sense of the living man himself. Francis is whimsical and affectionate and almost always in a hurry... he is at once excessively polite and bewilderingly abrupt; he is often very funny; he is generous almost to lunacy."
3. **Tartt's personal autobiographical account** (pp. viii–ix). Discloses that she "first became intrigued by St. Francis of Assisi when I was about fourteen years old, thanks to Zooey Glass's remark to Franny, in *Franny and Zooey*, that St. Francis was more loveable than Jesus." Describes her Mississippi childhood: "Growing up in a part of America stringently dominated by Christian fundamentalism, and not being sympathetic to it by either upbringing or temperament, I had come to believe with all my ninth-grade heart that all Christianity everywhere (ancient, modern, Catholic, protestant) was as suffocating and humorless as the evangelical bullying which was for me a dispiriting fact of life. (Perhaps other children were edified to learn that working mothers were destined for hell fire, or by being forced to wear black yarn tied around a finger signifying that they were 'against Christ,' but I was not one of them)."

**Cross-religion comparisons:** Tartt characterizes Francis as "very reminiscent of some of the great Buddhist saints and Boddhisatvas" and "probably the closest thing we have to a **bhakti or a sufi in the Western tradition**." Concludes with G.K. Chesterton's framing of Francis as "the court fool of the King of Paradise."

**Significance:** The foreword contains Tartt's most explicit published criticism of the fundamentalist religious culture in which she was raised. The "black yarn tied around a finger signifying they were 'against Christ'" reference is a vivid first-person datum about her PDS / Greenwood-Mississippi adolescence and a useful primary source for any biographical treatment of Tartt's religious background and its influence on her fiction (cf. the religious-mystic strand of *The Little Friend* and *The Goldfinch*'s closing meditation).

**Full-text source archived at:** `assets/sources/archive/excerpts/Tartt-Foreword-LifeStFrancis-2005-pp-v-ix.md`

**Chronology and significance:**
- Second-earliest confirmed Tartt foreword/introduction in this reference, after §7.1 (Charles Portis, *True Grit*, Bloomsbury UK reissue, January 17, 2005). Life of St. Francis follows by exactly fifteen days.
- §7.1 is the definitive earliest Tartt introduction with no outstanding earlier candidate.
- Thematically connects to Tartt's documented interest in religious mysticism (visible in *The Goldfinch*'s closing meditation, in her 2024 Reclaiming Art introduction §7.6, and in the Catholic-mystic strand of *The Little Friend*). The 2005 Life of St. Francis foreword is the earliest documented Tartt-authored statement on spiritual / religious subject matter.
- Multiple HarperCollins imprints have reprinted this volume (Harper San Francisco 2005; HarperOne 2009; HarperCollins later printings) — text is consistent across printings per dealer descriptions. The single ISBN 9780060576523 covers the body of printings.

**Canonical URLs:**
- HarperCollins product page: https://www.harpercollins.com/products/the-life-of-st-francis?variant=32117799419938
- Barnes & Noble: https://barnesandnoble.com/w/the-life-of-st-francis-bonaventure/1115065775
- Open Library (Bonaventure work): https://openlibrary.org/works/OL275055W

Full text extracted from `assets/sources/archive/LifeStFrancis-HarperCollinsSpiritualClassics-2005-9780060576523-AnnasArchive.pdf`.

**Foreword bibliographic detail:**
- **Page range: pp. v–[ix]** (Roman-numeral pagination, in front matter; precedes Prologue at p. 1)
- Volume total: 180 pages (per pdfinfo)
- Edition statement: FIRST EDITION (HarperSanFrancisco / HarperCollins Spiritual Classics)
- LC class: BX4700.F65E5 2005
- Dewey: 271'.302
- Editor: **Emilie Griffin** (HarperCollins Spiritual Classics series editor)
- Translation: Ewert Cousins (translation copyright © 1978 Paulist Press, Inc.)
- Foreword: © 2005 by Donna Tartt

**Tartt's foreword opening:** "*From the instant Francis Bernardone first stepped into the arms of the Bishop of Assissi and onto the field of history, he has been beloved by pagan and Christian alike. In fact, of all the saints, he is perhaps the greatest ambassador of the Church—the ideal introduction to Christianity for people of different faiths and cultures.*"

**Tartt's framing of Francis (cross-cultural mystic / bhakti / sufi reading):** "*Indeed Francis—in his sweetness and strength, in his unswerving compassion for all beings—is very reminiscent of some of the great Buddhist saints and Boddhisatvas, but he is also probably the closest thing we have to a bhakti or a sufi in the Western tradition. He is wholly uninterested in the outer trappings of dogma and ritual; what matters to him is inner devotion, the life of the heart.*"

**Tartt's biographical opening of her own connection to Francis:** "*For my part, I first became intrigued by St. Francis of Assissi when I was about fourteen years old, thanks to Zooey Glass's remark to Franny, in Franny and Zooey, that St. Francis was more loveable than Jesus.*" (Establishes the Salinger → Francis entry-point at age ~14, c. 1977–78.)

**Cited references in the foreword:** G.K. Chesterton (uncited edition) on Francis as "anticipat[ing] all that is most liberal and sympathetic in the modern mood"; Bonaventure's account of Francis's mission to the Soldan during the Crusades.

**Total foreword length estimate:** ~5–6 pages (pp. v through ix, possibly into x), ~1500–2000 words. Detailed Salinger-Glass family / Buddhist / sufi framing throughout.

### 7.24 Tartt childhood memoir — "encounter with a hummingbird" in *When We Were Young: A Compendium of Childhood*, compiled by John Burningham (Bloomsbury, 2005)

**Cover:** `assets/images/TARTT-CONTRIB-WhenWeWereYoung-Bloomsbury-2005_cover_openlibrary.jpg` — green cover with children-playing illustration.

**Bibliographic record:**

| Field | Data |
|---|---|
| Title | *When We Were Young: A Compendium of Childhood* |
| Compiler / Illustrator | **John Burningham** (1936–2019, English children's-book author, two-time Kate Greenaway Medal winner — *Borka*, *Mr Gumpy's Outing*) |
| Editor (per Amazon listing) | Rosemary Foot |
| Publisher | Bloomsbury Publishing PLC, London |
| Publication date | 2004 (per Internet Archive); September 1 / September 19, 2005 (paperback per Open Library + Bokus) |
| Format | Paperback (also hardcover); 312 pp |
| Dimensions | 5 × 1 × 7.75 in. (129 × 198 × 20 mm) |
| ISBN-13 | 978-0-7475-7663-1 |
| ISBN-10 | 0-7475-7663-7 |
| LCCN | 2005482102 |
| Cover price | £7.99 |
| Affiliated charity | UNICEF (cover-blurb) |
| Internet Archive | `whenwewereyoung0000burn` |

**Tartt's contribution:** A childhood-memoir prose piece described in the publisher's description and multiple dealer listings as **"Donna Tartt's affecting encounter with a hummingbird"** — a previously uncatalogued Tartt prose work. The framing as a "sighting" / "encounter" indicates an autobiographical childhood memory in the same family as her 1992 Harper's piece "Sleepytown" (§5.1) and her 2002 *Telegraph* interview (P15, O03).

Other named contributors in the volume: Michael Palin (seaside holidays with father), Seamus Heaney (crashed Cadbury's chocolate van), John Major (cricket-radio childhood), Sylvia Syms (loss of mother at age 12), Dirk Bogarde (a cinema encounter), Benjamin Zephaniah (childhood exposure of adult hypocrisy), Kofi Annan, Norman Lewis (Sunday-school facts-of-life lesson via steam-engine-driven dolls).

**Collecting significance:**
- First documented Tartt childhood-memoir prose piece since "Sleepytown" (1992). A 13-year gap between her two known autobiographical childhood pieces.
- Bloomsbury (UK) is the same publisher that issued *The Little Friend* (2002, §3.3) and the 2009 boxed signed limited (§2.7). The 2005 Burningham anthology falls in the post-TLF / pre-TG composition gap.
- The piece is illustrated by Burningham; the volume contains 50+ Burningham drawings.
- UNICEF-affiliated, which suggests the volume's contributors waived honoraria for charity.

**Canonical URLs:**
- Bloomsbury product page: https://www.bloomsbury.com/in/when-we-were-young-9780747576631/
- Open Library: https://openlibrary.org/books/OL7962696M
- Internet Archive (full scan): https://archive.org/details/whenwewereyoung0000burn
- Amazon: https://www.amazon.com/When-Were-Young-Compendium-Childhood/dp/0747576637
- Bokus (Swedish dealer with full description): https://www.bokus.com/bok/9780747576631/when-we-were-young

Full text extracted from `assets/sources/archive/WhenWeWereYoung-Burningham-Bloomsbury-2004-9780747571810-AnnasArchive.pdf`.

**Tartt piece bibliographic detail:**
- **Title:** The piece is **untitled** — the chapter heading is simply "DONNA TARTT" (in caps, top of p. 294). This is the structure of the entire volume: each contributor's piece appears under a chapter heading consisting of the contributor's name.
- **Page range:** **pp. 294–297** (chapter title page 294; prose pp. 295–297, ending mid-p. 297 where the next major section "The Land of Lost Content" begins with its own epigraphs from Barrie, Carroll, Stein, and Housman). Index entry: "Tartt, Donna 295" (citing the start of prose).
- Tartt's piece is the closing piece of the section preceding "The Land of Lost Content."
- Hardcover ISBN: 978-0-7475-7181-0 (this PDF copy — slightly different ISBN from the paperback ISBN 9780747576631 documented above; both are Bloomsbury 2004/2005 imprints)
- Total volume pages: 324
- **Editor credit (corrected):** "RESEARCH AND INTERVIEWS BY ROSE FOOT" — name is Rose Foot, not Rosemary Foot. The volume is "Compiled and illustrated by John Burningham" with research/interviews by Rose Foot.

**Editor's introduction mention of Tartt's piece:** Burningham's introduction explicitly highlights it — "Donna Tartt's sighting of a hummingbird and Benjamin Zephaniah's [piece]…" — singling it out as one of the memorable contributions, signed "John Burningham, London, July 2004."

**Contributor bio (page near the back of the volume):**
> DONNA TARTT b. 1963, Greenwood, Mississippi. Educated Bennington College, University of Mississippi. Writer. Novels include: The Secret History, The Little Friend. Lives in Virginia and New York City.

(Bio confirms Tartt's stated residence as **"Virginia and New York City"** as of 2004.)

**Tartt's piece — closing line:**
> "*All I know of the sublime is somehow encapsulated and encoded in that instant: flowers everywhere, white-gloved ladies in pastel dresses. Then beautiful Ginger, in an apple-green dress, kneeling to say hello.*"

**Cross-reference:** The "beloved great-grandmother" in this piece is the same great-grandmother who features in §7.19 (Fairy Tale Review Blue Issue 2005, "On Barrie and Stevenson") — born 1890 in Mississippi, Scottish ancestry, the reading-aloud companion. The two pieces (2004 and 2005) are companion autobiographical works centred on the same person.

**Full-text source archived at:** `assets/sources/archive/excerpts/Tartt-Hummingbird-WhenWeWereYoung-2004-pp294-297.md`

**Tartt's piece — full opening:**
"*Not long ago, my little godson came to stay with me for the first time: his first summer vacation, and also his first trip to the countryside. Though still an infant, not yet able to speak, his eyes were round and ringing with astonishment all weekend long. Everything at my house was shocking and utterly new: velvet sofa cushions, purple flowers, elderly pug (bigger than he was, a frightening but friendly lion).*"

**The hummingbird memory (core of the piece):**
"*The very earliest memory of my own life, and will be with me until I die, is of the first time I saw a hummingbird. The incident was inconsequential enough; I was about four years old, and had accompanied my beloved great-grandmother (then in her late seventies) to a garden party given for a distant relative: a young bride-to-be. It was springtime: the azaleas were in spectacular bloom; the astonishing little ruby-throated creature flew right in front of me — down at my eye level, practically in front of my face — and hovered there for some moments before it buzzed forward, then backward, then flew away across the green lawn for ever.*"

**Tartt's mid-life reflection (closing meditation):**
"*Only now — at mid-life, in my fortieth year — am I starting to realize what the hummingbird means, and why — at unexpected moments — it returns to me still. It is a premonition of Heaven, and of Death. My great-grandmother (who was leaning beside me, holding my hand, as the hummingbird paused in mid-air before me) did not have long to live. Nor did the bride herself — lovely laughing Ginger, who died young, of cancer.*"

**Dating the piece:** Tartt born December 23, 1963. "In my fortieth year" = 2003–2004 (her 40th birthday was Dec 23, 2003). Bloomsbury volume was published 2004. Tartt wrote this piece specifically for the Burningham anthology, in 2003–2004 — not a reprint, an original commission.

**Cross-references inside the reference:**
- Same great-grandmother appears in §7.19 (FT Blue Issue "On Barrie and Stevenson," 2005) — born 1890 in Mississippi, lived there her whole life, the reading-aloud companion.
- Same Mississippi springtime / azalea imagery as in TLF (cf. *The Little Friend*, 2002).
- "Lovely laughing Ginger, who died young, of cancer" — a biographical detail about a young Mississippi woman (a "distant relative" / bride-to-be) who knew the toddler Tartt.
- "Elderly pug (bigger than he was, a frightening but friendly lion)" — the Tartt pug Pongo (born ~1987, see USA Today 2002 interview O09).

**Theme:** Premonition of Heaven and Death; the hummingbird as iridescent emblem of mutability and the brevity of life. Same theme-cluster as Tartt's later closing-meditation passages in *The Goldfinch* (2013).

**Other contributors observed in the volume:** Michael Palin (seaside), Seamus Heaney (Cadbury's chocolate van), John Major (cricket-radio), Sylvia Syms (loss of mother at 12), Dirk Bogarde (cinema), Benjamin Zephaniah (adult hypocrisy), Kofi Annan, Norman Lewis, Posy Simmonds ("The Land of Lost Content"). The volume is illustrated by Burningham himself (chapter-opening line drawings).

### 7.25 Tartt featured in *Legendary Authors and the Clothes They Wore* by Terry Newman (Harper Design / HarperCollins, 2017)

**Cover:** *(no cover image currently available)*

Tartt is one of the featured authors; the chapter integrates first-person Tartt quotations and a curated style biography.

**Bibliographic record:**

| Field | Data |
|---|---|
| Title | *Legendary Authors and the Clothes They Wore* |
| Author | **Terry Newman** (London-based fashion journalist — former editor at *i-D*, *Attitude*, *Self Service*; lecturer, University for the Creative Arts, Epsom) |
| Publisher | Harper Design / HarperCollins Publishers, New York |
| Publication date | June 27, 2017 |
| Format | Hardcover, 207 pp |
| ISBN-13 | 978-0-06-242830-1 (hc) / 978-0-06-242831-8 (e-book) |
| ISBN-10 | 0-06-242830-6 (hc) / 0-06-242831-4 (e-book) |
| Featured authors (50 total) | Donna Tartt + Maya Angelou, Truman Capote, Colette, Bret Easton Ellis, Allen Ginsberg, Patti Smith, Karl Ove Knausgaard, David Foster Wallace, Quentin Crisp, Simone de Beauvoir, T.S. Eliot, F. Scott + Zelda Fitzgerald, Malcolm Gladwell, John Updike, Oscar Wilde, Tom Wolfe, Samuel Beckett, James Joyce, Joan Didion, Edith Sitwell, Hunter S. Thompson, Virginia Woolf, Nancy Mitford, Sylvia Plath, Susan Sontag, Toni Morrison, William Burroughs, Joe Orton, Marcel Proust, Gertrude Stein, Zadie Smith, George Sand, Djuna Barnes, Fran Lebowitz, Jacqueline Susann, Dorothy Parker, Arthur Rimbaud, others |

**Tartt's contribution:** A ~940-word style-profile chapter, opening with the epigraph quotation *"Very nice clothes are not incompatible with the writer's profession in a way that they are for a painter or a dancer"* (sourced "This Much I Know," The Guardian / Observer Magazine 2003 — corresponds to MAG-018 in this reference). The chapter integrates: (a) biographical narrative from TSH 1992 through TG 2013 with publication dates and themes; (b) four first-person Tartt quotations (see "Quotations cited" below); (c) two archival photographs (see "Photographs" below); (d) a long *Secret History* excerpt (Bunny's mocking of Richard's "Western cut" clothes) used as in-prose example; and (e) curated trivia (Tartt's hair styled à la Louise Brooks / Agatha Runcible from Waugh's *Vile Bodies*; "She likes to wear suits"; Tartt as a fan of Pulp and The White Stripes; childhood reading = *Peter Pan* and *Treasure Island*). The chapter text is archived at `assets/sources/archive/excerpts/Tartt-LegendaryAuthorsClothes-Newman-2017-ch31.md`.

**Quotations from Tartt cited in the Newman chapter (4 total):**
1. *"Very nice clothes are not incompatible with the writer's profession in a way that they are for a painter or a dancer."* — credited "This Much I Know," *The Guardian*, 2003 [= MAG-018, the *OM Observer* 16 November 2003 column].
2. *"I feel a real funniness about women's costume. To really put on high heels and a frilly dress, do you know what I'm saying? It seems kind of . . . comical."* — credited to a 2002 *Telegraph* interview (likely P15, Mick Brown).
3. *"I'd love to meet Oscar Wilde, because they all say he was so much more wonderful in person than on the page… And if it was a dinner date? Albert Camus. That trench coat! That cigarette! I think my French is good enough. We'd have a great time."* — credited "Donna Tartt: By the Book," *NYT Book Review*, **2013** [= §7.16; canonical date October 20, 2013].
4. *"I get very attached to coats because a coat is a comfort, you can curl up with it. I bought a beautiful cashmere coat about ten years ago and I love it. It's really like my security blanket."* — credited "This Much I Know," 2003.

**Photographs of Tartt in the chapter (2 total):**
1. **"Donna Tartt, 2014."** by **Susanna Howe** — credited Trunk Archive.
2. **"Donna Tartt, circa 2000."** by **Timothy Greenfield-Sanders** — the portrait photographer (NYRB documentary subject).

**Collecting significance:**
- The first documented book-length appearance of Tartt as a style/fashion subject. Tartt's tailoring (often noted in interviews — bespoke menswear-influenced suits, white shirts, jet-black bob — see P10 Tonkin 2002, P15 Brown 2002, and the September 1992 promotional photo cluster) has been a recurring theme in her press coverage; this is the first treatment of it as a primary subject of a published book.
- Other contemporary Tartt-related figures in the volume: Bret Easton Ellis (Bennington classmate, original TSH introduction-maker), Arthur Rimbaud (whom Tartt translated for *Fairy Tale Review* Green Issue, §7.22).
- Co-published as e-book by Open Road Media (ISBN 9780062428318).

**Canonical URLs:**
- HarperCollins Canada product page: https://www.harpercollins.ca/9780062428301/legendary-authors-and-the-clothes-they-wore/
- Open Road Media: https://openroadmedia.com/ebook/legendary-authors-and-the-clothes-they-wore/9780062428318
- The Cut review (Sarah Spellings, 2017-06-26): https://www.thecut.com/2017/06/dissecting-the-personal-style-of-the-greatest-writers.html
- PORT Magazine review: https://www.port-magazine.com/fashion/legendary-authors-and-they-clothes-they-wore/

TOC placement extracted from `assets/sources/archive/LegendaryAuthorsClothes-Newman-HarperDesign-2017-9780062428301-AnnasArchive.epub`.

**Tartt's position in the volume:** Tartt is the **31st chapter**, between Ernest Hemingway (Ch. 30) and Colette (Ch. 32). The volume's TOC sequence opens with Samuel Beckett, George Sand, John Updike, Arthur Rimbaud, Gertrude Stein, Patti Smith, etc. Tartt's chapter sits in the second half of the volume. Approximate page range based on 940-word chapter length, position 31 of ~55 chapters at ~4 pp each, and 207-page total: **estimated pp. ~125–129** (precise pp. need physical copy since the EPUB strips printed page numbers).

**Significance:** Of the named 21st-century novelists in the volume, Tartt and Zadie Smith are the principal examples; Newman positions Tartt's bespoke menswear-influenced suiting alongside Wilde's velvet, Capote's haunted-houses uniform, Didion's understatement, and Joyce's eyepatched dandyism.

The complete Tartt-profile text, archival photography references, and quotation content can be read from `LegendaryAuthorsClothes-Newman-HarperDesign-2017-9780062428301-AnnasArchive.epub`.

### 7.26 Tartt portrait in *A Portrait of Southern Writers* by Curt Richter (Hill Street Press, 2000) — photograph commissioned by the Fellowship of Southern Writers

**Cover:** `assets/images/TARTT-CONTRIB-PortraitSouthernWriters-Richter-2000_cover_abebooks.jpg` — front cover showing four author portraits in 2×2 grid.

Curt Richter's official portfolio page lists Donna Tartt with location "New York City, Winter 1996" alongside ~20 other photographed Southern writers.

**Bibliographic record:**

| Field | Data |
|---|---|
| Title | *A Portrait of Southern Writers* |
| Author (photographer) | **Curt P. Richter** (8×10 Toyo M view camera, Nikkor-Apo 300mm f/9 lens, Tri-X film) |
| Foreword | Robert Coles |
| Afterword | Ann Beattie |
| Commissioning body | Louis D. Rubin, Jr. / **Fellowship of Southern Writers** — initial 28 founding members |
| Supporting bodies | Guggenheim Foundation Fellowship; National Endowment of the Humanities; National Endowment of the Arts; U.S. Information Agency (traveling exhibition) |
| Publisher | Hill Street Press, LLC, Athens, GA |
| Publication date | 2000 |
| Format | Hardcover with dust jacket, quarto |
| ISBN-13 | 978-1-892514-83-7 |
| ISBN-10 | 1-892514-83-4 |
| Goodreads rating | 4.60 / 5 (5 ratings) |
| Total photographs | ~100 images of "over 200 writers associated with the South" photographed over a 7-year period (1989–1996) |

**Tartt's appearance:** A formal black-and-white 8×10 portrait of Donna Tartt taken by Curt Richter in **New York City, Winter 1996**. The portrait is also issued as a **limited edition of 25 platinum/palladium prints**, available for sale via direct contact with the artist. This makes the Tartt portrait a documented standalone fine-art collectible apart from the book context.

Other major Tartt-adjacent subjects photographed: Eudora Welty (1989, first sitter), Alice Walker (1996, last sitter), William Styron (1989), Ralph Ellison (1990), Walker Percy (1995), Albert Murray (1994), Shelby Foote (1995), Jimmy Carter (1995), Reynolds Price (1989), Harry Crews (1995), Beth Henley (1995), James Dickey, Ann Beattie (1995), Bailey White (1995), Jonathan Williams (1994), Tim McLaurin (1995), William Baldwin (1995), Hunt Hawkins (1995), Ishmael Reed (1996).

**Collecting significance:**
- The first documented Tartt portrait in a published photo monograph. Other Tartt photography of comparable provenance: the September 1992 Henry Benson "Smart Tartt" *Vanity Fair* portraits (§8.1) and the Mark Coles 2001 BBC *Today* (audio-only).
- The 25-copy platinum/palladium limited-edition print of the Tartt portrait is a documented Tartt collectible. Platinum/palladium printing is the most archival photo-print process. (Richter directs interested collectors to contact him directly.)
- Hill Street Press is a small Athens, GA literary publisher; the 2000 first edition with dust jacket is the standard collecting state.
- The associated traveling exhibition (NEH/NEA/USIA-supported) suggests catalog material may exist separately; not yet documented in this reference.

**Canonical URLs:**
- Curt Richter portfolio (Tartt portrait on the page): https://www.curtrichter.com/a-portrait-of-southern-writers
- AbeBooks listing: https://www.abebooks.com/first-edition/Portrait-Southern-Writers-Richter-Curt-P/210221800/bd
- Fellowship of Southern Writers: https://www.fellowshipofsouthernwriters.org/

### 7.27 Tartt letter — *Livraison N°2* (Marie Birde ed., Stockholm, 2006–2007) — themed letter-writing issue

**Cover:** `assets/images/TARTT-CONTRIB-Livraison-No2-2006_cover_scan.jpg` — black background, large photo of a white plaster/clay finger suspended above a pink-filled spoon-shaped vessel; spine-tag at left reads "Livraison" in blackletter script; lower-left masthead "LIVRAISON / N°2 / EXCHANGE ISSUE / HIDDEN OBJECTS / 2006/2007". *(Supersedes the Dashwood placeholder.)*

**Bibliographic record:**

| Field | Data |
|---|---|
| Title | *Livraison N°2* (themed "letter-writing" issue) |
| Editor | **Marie Birde** (Swedish journalist; founder of *Darling* magazine 1996; later contributor to *Stil* (P1), editor of *Koko*, author of *Vintage: en stilguide till vintagemode*) |
| Publisher | Livraison (Stockholm) |
| Publication date | 2006–2007 |
| Format | Softcover, 230 × 330 mm (oversize), 378 pp |
| Print run | **1,500 copies** |
| ISBN | 9197563307 (note: bokbörsen mistakenly applies this ISBN to N°1 also — Dashwood's listing makes N°2 attribution definitive) |

**Tartt's contribution:** A single letter exchanged with the magazine, in response to a letter from the magazine's editorial team. Per the publisher's description: "Letters are not the obvious inspiration in a world currently inundated with ways to keep in touch at all times (e-mail, mobile telephones, text messages, blackberries)... This issue is about rediscovering the art of letterwriting. How did the people we were intrigued by react to our letters? Heroes and heroines like Miranda July, **Donna Tartt**, Julie Verhoeven, Alexander Robotnick, Michael Nyman, Carl Johan de Geer, Jonas Hassen Khemiri, Wes Lang, Alain de Botton and Serena Reeder exchanged a single letter each in reply to ours."

Tartt's letter is a single original reply-letter to the Livraison editorial team — first published in this issue and not reprinted elsewhere.

**Physical examination:** Full text is held at `assets/sources/archive/excerpts/Tartt-Livraison-No2-2006-AnonymousPartygoer-letter.pdf` (5 pages including front cover, title spread, the letter page, and the masthead/credits last-page spread). Tartt's letter appears on **p. 145** of the magazine. Salutation **"Dear Anonymous Partygoer,"** with the magazine's "FIRST PAGE >>" / "LAST PAGE >>" page markers framing the issue. The letter is **dated 2005-11-09** in the dateline. Tartt describes herself answering "on the back of a travel itinerary, on an airplane" and discusses: in-flight reading (Joseph Conrad's *Victory*, Ian Rankin's *Black and Blue*, Arthur Rimbaud — whose "prose poems and the collected poems… are going to be published in the next issue of a magazine called >>Fairy Tale Review<<" — a direct primary-source confirmation of §7.22, the *Fairy Tale Review* Vol 2 Green Issue 2006 Rimbaud translations); music (Death in Vegas's *The Contino Sessions*); cinema and TV (Christian Bale, Michael Caine, *Sex and the City*, *Absolutely Fabulous* — favorite episode "Door Handle"); travel (two Bonnier parties in Sweden "a decade apart" — once for the TSH first book tour, once "in Sweden for the second"); her opinions on the painter Giorgio Morandi (revised from "monotonous and dull" to "very important to me"); influences/aversions (Nabokov, Hitchcock, Bradbury, Homer, Aeschylus, Dickens, Proust, T.S. Eliot, Virginia Woolf, John Milton; Saul Bellow described as leaving her "cold"); a Caldecott-Medal anecdote about her childhood reading aversion to "official literary context" books. Masthead credits (last page): Editor in Chief **Marie Birde**; Art Direction Henrik Timonen, Johan Sandberg; Editor Elizabeth Clark Vessel; Printing House Wassbergs + Skotte Tryckeri (Falun, Sweden); Pre Press Linjepunkt (Falun); Paper Munken Print 300g & 150g (Arctic Paper, Göteborg); Cover by Béla Borsodi; **Printed in Sweden, ISBN 91-975633-0-7, Livraison ©2006**.

Other "word contributors" listed in the issue: Alain de Botton, Alexander Robotnick, Alysa Nahmias, Amy Kellner, Andreas Tilliander, Anna Lundh, Aresa, Belles of the Black Diamondfield, Bennett Madison, Billy Parish, Carl Johan de Geer, **Donna Tartt**, Emily Barclay, Field, Geneviève Gauckler, Hassan Khan, Jonas Hassen Khemiri, Jordan Schuster, Juan Maclean, Julie Verhoeven, Kim Jones, Malte Schlorf, Mark Doty, Matti Pyykko, Michael Nyman, Miranda July, Misaki Kawai, Naoyuki Tsuji, Paola Stenborg, Serena Reeder, Tetsuya Mizuguchi, the Magic Numbers, the Yes Men, Reiko Underwater, Roger Andersson, Ruben Fleischer, Wes Lang, Yasmine Kassari.

**Collecting significance:**
- A previously uncatalogued Tartt-authored prose piece in letter form. Tartt's known correspondence is exceedingly thin in the published record — this is one of very few documented Tartt letters in any public-facing print form.
- 1,500-copy print run plus oversized format (230 × 330 mm, 378 pp) plus 2006–2007 publication date (post-TLF, mid-TG composition) makes this a niche but distinctive collecting target.
- Out-of-print and described by Dashwood Books as "difficult to find."
- Companion: *Livraison N°1* (Private Issue, 2005, Marie Birde) does NOT include Tartt — that issue is interview/portrait themed; named contributors are Andreas Larsson, Ola Rindal, Bruce Labruce, Jason Lee, Maison Martin Margiela, Matthew Thurber, Asia Argento.

**Canonical URLs:**
- Livraison.se: https://www.livraison.se/
- Dashwood Books listing for N°2 (with full description): https://dashwoodbooks.com/pages/books/19626/livraison-no-2
- Bokbörsen N°1 listing (note: ISBN attribution issue): https://www.bokborsen.se/view/-/Livraison-Private-Issue-No-1-This-Magazine-I/6192082
- Open Book Collectibles N°1 listing: https://www.openbookcollectibles.com/shop/p/livraison-magazine-1-private-issue

Tartt's letter is a single-page reply-letter dated 2005-11-09, salutation "Dear Anonymous Partygoer", appearing on p. 145 of Livraison N°2 (ISBN 91-975633-0-7, Stockholm 2006). Full text captured at `assets/sources/archive/excerpts/Tartt-Livraison-No2-2006-AnonymousPartygoer-letter.pdf`.

---

### 7.28 Tartt essay "On True Grit" reprinted — *Escape Velocity: A Charles Portis Miscellany*, ed. Jay Jennings (Butler Center Books / Overlook Press, 2012–2013); revised edition with new Tartt afterword (University of Arkansas Press, 2021)

The 2012/2013 first edition reprints Tartt's 2005 True Grit introduction (§7.1) in the Appendix: Tributes. The 2021 revised edition adds a second, distinct Tartt text — a new afterword adapted from her 2020 NYT Portis tribute (§6.6). Two separate Tartt appearances across two editions of the same volume.

**Bibliographic record — all editions:**

| Edition | Publisher | Date | ISBN | Format | Tartt content |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| First edition | Butler Center for Arkansas Studies (Butler Center Books) | October 2012 | 978-1-935106-50-0 | Hardcover, 380 pp | "On True Grit" (Appendix: Tributes) — reprint of §7.1 |
| Overlook Press reissue | Overlook Press (New York) / Duckworth (London) | 2013 | 978-1-4683-0849-5 | Paperback | Same — "On True Grit" (Appendix: Tributes) |
| Revised edition | University of Arkansas Press / Butler Center Books | August 2021 | 978-1-945624-26-1 (cloth) | Cloth | New afterword by Donna Tartt (adapted from §6.6 NYT 2020) |

**Editor:** Jay Jennings. **Publisher of record for revised edition:** Butler Center for Arkansas Studies / University of Arkansas Press (distributed).

---

**Tartt contribution — First edition / Overlook reissue:**

Title as printed: **"On True Grit"** (chapter heading). Positioned in: **Appendix: Tributes** — the final section of the book, after the main Portis texts, the epilogue interview, and before the Sources and Acknowledgements.

Nature of text: This is a **reprint** of Tartt's introduction to the Bloomsbury 2005 UK reissue of *True Grit* (§7.1). The acknowledgements page confirms: "The authors of the appreciations in the appendix — Roy Blount Jr., Ed Park, Ron Rosenbaum, Donna Tartt, and Wells Tower — get great appreciation in turn from me for their eagerness to allow their work to be **reprinted here**." The text is identical to the essay confirmed via the Overlook 2010 True Grit EPUB (§7.1, ~2,915 words); EPUB extraction from the Overlook 2013 *Escape Velocity* EPUB yields **~2,924 words** — negligibly different, consistent with the same text across two slightly different digital transcriptions.

**Contributor bio note as printed:** *"Donna Tartt is the author of the novels* The Secret History *(1992) and* The Little Friend *(2002)."* — Pre-*Goldfinch* (2013) wording, consistent with the essay having been commissioned in 2004–2005 for the Bloomsbury reissue. No update was made to the bio note for the 2013 Overlook reissue.

**Structural position in the Appendix:** Tartt's piece is the fourth of five tributes, between Ron Rosenbaum's "Our Least-Known Great Novelist" and Wells Tower's "The Book That Changed My Life: *Gringos*." Full tribute sequence:
1. Roy Blount Jr. — "Comedy in Earnest"
2. Ed Park — "Like Cormac McCarthy, but Funny"
3. Ron Rosenbaum — "Our Least-Known Great Novelist"
4. **Donna Tartt — "On True Grit"**
5. Wells Tower — "The Book That Changed My Life: *Gringos*"

**EPUB confirmation:** Full text confirmed via EPUB at `assets/sources/archive/EscapeVelocity-Portis-OverlookPress-2013-9781468308495-AnnaArchive.epub`. Tartt essay at `OEBPS/Text/chapter022.html`. Text opens: *"It's commonplace to say that we 'love' a book, but when we say it, we really mean all sorts of things…"* Closes: *"Now — thankfully — the book is back in print, and I am delighted to have the honor of introducing Mattie Ross and Rooster Cogburn to a new generation of readers."* Full text identical to §7.1 canonical text confirmed via Brick Magazine (https://brickmag.com/the-great-abiding-pleasure-of-true-grit/) and the Overlook 2010 *True Grit* EPUB.

---

**Tartt contribution — Revised edition (University of Arkansas Press, 2021):**

Title as printed: **Afterword** (by Donna Tartt). Nature of text: A new, distinct Tartt text — not the 2005 True Grit introduction. Per the UA Press product page: "This revised edition includes a new afterword by best-selling author Donna Tartt, who first published her remembrance in the *New York Times* following Portis's death in 2020." This afterword is an adaptation of §6.6 (Tartt, "Donna Tartt on the Singular Voice, and Pungent Humor, of Charles Portis," *NYT Book Review*, June 9, 2020; print edition June 28, 2020 retitled "True Grit"). Whether the 2021 afterword is identical to the 2020 NYT text or a revised/expanded version is not established.

The 2021 afterword is not in the Overlook 2013 EPUB. Collectors seeking the 2021 Tartt text must acquire the UA Press revised edition (ISBN 978-1-945624-26-1).

---

**Collecting significance:**

- The **first edition (Butler Center Books, 2012, ISBN 978-1-935106-50-0)** is the first print publication of this Tartt text in an American hardcover anthology — the Bloomsbury 2005 UK introduction had not previously appeared in a US hardcover context.
- The **Overlook 2013 paperback** is more readily found on the secondary market and documents the same Tartt essay text.
- The **2021 UA Press revised edition** is the only print venue for Tartt's second Portis essay text (the 2020 NYT tribute adapted as afterword) — a distinct collecting target from the 2012/2013 editions.
- The Overlook 2013 ad-card documents Tartt's afterword across multiple Overlook True Grit sub-editions: "It is available from Overlook in a movie tie-in edition and a mass market edition, both of which include an afterword by Donna Tartt, as well as a young readers edition, with an afterword by Leonard S. Marcus." This confirms the Tartt True Grit essay circulated in at minimum three distinct Overlook True Grit formats (movie tie-in, mass market, and the 2010 reprint EPUB at §7.1) in addition to the Bloomsbury UK 2005 first appearance.

**File archival:** `assets/sources/archive/EscapeVelocity-Portis-OverlookPress-2013-9781468308495-AnnaArchive.epub`

**Canonical URLs:**
- UA Press product page (revised edition): https://www.uapress.com/product/escape-velocity/
- Butler Center blog (2012 launch announcement): https://butlercenter.blogspot.com/2012/10/escape-velocity-charles-portis.html
- AbeBooks (first edition, ISBN 9781935106500): https://www.abebooks.com/9781935106500/
- Goodreads editions list: https://www.goodreads.com/work/editions/21655171-escape-velocity-a-charles-portis-miscellany
- Roberts Library blog (2021 revised edition announcement): https://robertslibrary.org/blog/escape-velocity-now-in-a-revised-edition/

**Cross-references:**
- §7.1 — the same "On True Grit" essay text in its original home (Bloomsbury 2005 introduction / Overlook 2010 afterword)
- §6.6 — the 2020 NYT Portis tribute that forms the basis of the 2021 revised edition afterword
- §7.2 — the Recorded Books 2006 True Grit audiobook (Tartt narrator + essay as afterword)

## 8. Press, ephemera, and the Lenox Hill chapbook program

### 8.1 Vanity Fair September 1992 — "Smart Tartt" by James Kaplan

Article: "Smart Tartt" by James Kaplan, Vanity Fair, September 1992. Photographer: Henry Benson. Subhead: "Every so often a first-novelist leaps out of the fray…" Key facts confirmed from the full article body: (1) the Knopf manuscript was 866 pages; (2) Bret Easton Ellis introduced Tartt to agent Amanda Urban at ICM, forming the acquisition chain that led to Sonny Mehta and Gary Fisketjon at Knopf; (3) the Knopf advance was $450,000. [94]

**Cover:** `assets/images/magazines/VF-1992-09-cover.jpg` — `EPH-001` (Vanity Fair September 1992 - Smart Tartt by Kaplan)

The opening photograph shows Tartt in dark sunglasses with her pug, Pongo. According to the Esther Fein NYT piece (November 16, 1992), Tina Brown — then editor-in-chief of Vanity Fair — commissioned this profile after Amanda Urban told her at a July 1992 lunch that Tartt was the new "hot" author. The article was part of a coordinated September 1992 promotional storm with feature-length pieces also appearing in Esquire, Mirabella, M, Cosmopolitan, Glamour, and Elle.

Bibliographic note (the goldfinch detail): in the final paragraph of the 1992 Kaplan profile, twenty-one years before publication of The Goldfinch, Tartt describes goldfinches as her favorite bird — "Look at these goldfinches… Goldfinches are the greatest little birds, because they build their nests in the spring, a long time after all the other birds do. They're the last to settle down — they just fly around and they're happy for a long time, and just sing and play. And only when it's insanely late in the year, they kind of break down and build their nests. I love goldfinches… they're my favorite bird." The detail was noted in subsequent reception of the 2013 novel as "prescient." The 1992 Vanity Fair issue is therefore a primary-source artefact of unusual collectible value.

![Fig. 8.1 — Vanity Fair, September 1992. Cover: Geena Davis, photographed by Michel Comte. The issue contains "Smart Tartt" by James Kaplan (photographer: Henry Benson), the landmark TSH launch profile that closes with Tartt's goldfinch passage. Cover: © Condé Nast / Michel Comte. Image: FashionModelDirectory.com.](assets/images/magazines/VF-1992-09-cover.jpg "Fig. 8.1 — Vanity Fair September 1992 — Geena Davis cover, contains 'Smart Tartt' by James Kaplan")

*Fig. 8.1 — Vanity Fair, September 1992 (cover: Geena Davis / Michel Comte). Contains "Smart Tartt" by James Kaplan — the primary-source TSH launch profile with the goldfinch-favourite-bird passage.*

### 8.2 The Bookseller (UK), 2002

"Donna Tartt: The child who read too much," by Benedicte Page, The Bookseller, June 27, 2002 (Author Interviews section). Tartt's first interview about The Little Friend, conducted by phone with Tartt at her home in Virginia, ahead of the October 28, 2002 UK launch (and the October 22, 2002 US Knopf publication). [14]

**Covers:**
- **EPH-002** — The Bookseller (UK) June 27 2002: *[no standalone cover — see source publication]*
- **EPH-002b** — The Bookseller (UK) Sept 26 2002 - Embargoes under pressure: *[no standalone cover — see source publication]*

Key facts captured by the Bookseller piece (substantial corroboration of publishing-context narrative):

  - $450,000 Knopf TSH advance reaffirmed ("a then extraordinary $450,000 advance from Knopf")

  - Penguin published TSH in the UK (paperback edition)

  - TLF UK pub data: October 28, 2002, ISBN 0747562113, £16.99, Bloomsbury

  - Bloomsbury's reported UK advance for TLF: £1M "rumoured price tag" — described in the Bookseller article as "believed to be overstated" but "the price was certainly high"

  - Tartt voluntarily withdrew from public view between novels: "It is the process of writing the book that fascinates her more than the achievement of the final novel"

  - Tartt's own description of the writing pace: "You can try to commodify writing, you can try to regulate it and make people turn it out, but in the end it is a process that is kind of organic. There are some flowers that only bloom every two years."

Companion Bookseller piece (September 2002): "Embargoes under pressure" by Richard Lewis — documents Bloomsbury's strict contractual sale ban for The Little Friend before October 28, 2002 publication, including David Ward (Bloomsbury sales director) noting that the publisher "would not baulk at imposing sanctions on retailers who flouted the ban" and had "taken action" against embargo-busters previously. This is unusual for literary fiction (more typical of high-volume titles like Harry Potter); it documents the magnitude of UK publishing-trade investment in the TLF launch. [15]

### 8.3 Lenox Hill Bookstore signed limited chapbook program (2004)

**Cover:** `assets/images/LENOX-CHAPBOOK-bib_9742eb47f0.jpg` — `EPH-003` (Lenox Hill chapbook 'Tam O'Shanter' 250 copies signed 2004)

See §5.2. [28]

### 8.4 Promotional posters and pre-publication ephemera

**Covers:**
- **EPH-004** — Esquire September 1992 'Tartt's Sweet Deal': `assets/images/magazines/ESQUIRE-1992-09-cover.jpg`
- **EPH-005** — Newsweek September 7 1992 'Anatomy of a Hype': `assets/images/_retrieved/EPH-005-newsweek-1992-alt.webp`
- **EPH-006** — Vogue September 1992 (Claudia Schiffer by Arthur Elgort): `assets/images/magazines/VOGUE-1992-09-cover_archive.jpg`
- **EPH-007** — Cosmopolitan September 1992: `assets/images/magazines/COSMO-1992-09-cover_archive.jpg`
- **EPH-008** — Glamour September 1992: `assets/images/magazines/GLAMOUR-1992-09-cover_archive.jpg`

Identified 1992 promotional ephemera:

  - AP wire / press-release photograph by Caitlin McCaffrey – used on the TSH US Knopf 1992 first-edition dust-jacket rear flap. The McCaffrey photograph is the most widely-distributed 1992 Tartt promotional image and was syndicated across newspaper coverage of the launch.

  - September 1992 coordinated magazine coverage: Tartt feature pieces and "sassy pictures" in multiple publications simultaneously. The Newsweek "Anatomy of a Hype" article (Laura Shapiro & Ray Sawhill, September 7, 1992) is itself a contemporary primary source that names six publications: "Tartt, 28, is featured in the latest issues of Vanity Fair, M, Esquire, Vogue, Elle and Mirabella." [Source: S080] [95]. The Fein NYT article (November 16, 1992) says "seven publications" and names Vanity Fair, Mirabella, M, Cosmopolitan, Glamour, Elle, Esquire. The two lists overlap substantially but differ on Vogue (Newsweek) vs. Cosmopolitan/Glamour (Fein). The Baffler (March 1993) further mentions "Mirabella, People, Entertainment Weekly, Vanity Fair, Esquire" [Source: S081]. Individual verification: (1) Vanity Fair September 1992 (§8.1; "Smart Tartt" by James Kaplan, photographer Henry Benson; full article confirmed; the goldfinch-closing-paragraph drives post-2014 demand); (2) Esquire September 1992 (Fein NYT + Newsweek Sept 7, 1992 + article text confirmed via Esquire Classic archive and languageisavirus.com reprint; title: "Tartt's Sweet Deal," authors: Anita LeClerc and Joseph Hooper, section: Man at His Best, September 1992 [Sources: S085, S086] [96]; Lili Anolik's Bennington oral-history work was a separate 2019 Esquire piece, not 1992);

![Fig. 8.2 — Esquire, September 1992. Cover: Robert Redford. Contains "Tartt's Sweet Deal" by Anita LeClerc and Joseph Hooper (section: Man at His Best) — one of the seven coordinated September 1992 Tartt launch profiles. Image: FashionModelDirectory.com.](assets/images/magazines/ESQUIRE-1992-09-cover-fmd.jpg "Fig. 8.2 — Esquire September 1992 — Robert Redford cover")

*Fig. 8.2 — Esquire, September 1992 (cover: Robert Redford). Contains "Tartt's Sweet Deal" by LeClerc & Hooper.* (3) Mirabella September 1992 (Fein NYT + Newsweek Sept 7, 1992 + Baffler March 1993; Mirabella magazine 1989–2000, now defunct); (4) M Magazine September 1992 (Fein NYT + Newsweek Sept 7, 1992; M was a Fairchild / Gentleman's Quarterly spin-off, short-lived); (5) Vogue September 1992 (Newsweek Sept 7, 1992 + The Times UK Oct 2002 profile mentions "Vanity Fair, Esquire, Vogue and Elle"; NOT listed in Fein NYT); (6) Cosmopolitan September 1992 (Fein NYT only; not in Newsweek list; not independently confirmed in dealer or archive record); (7) Glamour September 1992 (Fein NYT only; not in Newsweek list; not independently confirmed); (8) Elle September 1992 (Fein NYT + Newsweek Sept 7, 1992). The Fein "seven publications" figure may count differently than the Newsweek six; Vogue is likely one of the seven even if not named by Fein; it is possible Cosmopolitan and/or Glamour are conflations or that coverage was broader than either source alone captures. None of the non-Vanity Fair September 1992 issues are catalogued by ABAA-tier dealers as Tartt-related collectibles; their value, if any, would be as completist items.

  - Square Books, Oxford, MS – the September 17, 1992 launch signing is the canonical Tartt hometown launch event. No printed flier, poster, or signed-bookplate distribution from this 1992 event has surfaced in dealer infrastructure. The 2002 TLF Square Books / Thacker Mountain Radio Show signing (November 14, 2002) is documented in the Ole Miss archive (MUM00441 finding aid). The 1992 event remains under-documented.

  - Knopf 1992 ARC dust-jacket variants – the US Knopf advance state in glossy paper wrappers is documented (§2.3); a separate trade-show or BEA promotional variant has not been identified beyond the standard ARC.

  - Random House / Knopf 1992 promotional press kit – no catalogued copy located.

  - Knopf in-house Christmas / promotional booklets featuring TSH – see §8.5: the Borzoi Reader Vol 4 No 3 (Fall 1992) is Knopf's seasonal in-house catalog and contains a pre-publication excerpt of TSH on p. 7.

  - Bret Easton Ellis dedication-related ephemera – Ellis's own launch events and publicity for Less Than Zero (1985) and American Psycho (1991) overlapped with Tartt's Bennington years but no Tartt-related ephemera from Ellis's launch events has surfaced.

Identified 2002 promotional ephemera:

  - Bloomsbury TLF UK strict-embargo memo (Bookseller, September 2002, Richard Lewis) – documented in §8.2; the embargo memo is a publishing-trade artefact, not a collectible item.

  - Thacker Mountain Radio Show flyer (Oxford, MS, November 14, 2002) – held in the Ole Miss MUM00441 archive (§10.3); this is a primary-source flier confirmed in institutional inventory.

Identified 2013 promotional ephemera:

  - Powell's Indiespensable Volume 43 (October 2013) – boxed set (trade hardcover + brown cloth slipcase + signed letterpress chapbook). The chapbook is itself ephemera; signed in purple ink. Photograph embedded at §4.6.

  - Foyles signed first (UK 2013) – red sticker on jacket; signed in copper ink.

  - B\&N Signed First – bookplate variant; signed in brown ink.

Auction-house ephemera surveys:

  - Heritage Auctions – manual browse via title-search returned no Tartt-specific ephemera lots distinct from the bundled-multi-author lots in §10.1 (Lots \#90066 / 90068 / 90069 in Auction \#201135).

  - Swann Galleries – search returned no Tartt-specific ephemera.

  - PBA Galleries – no Tartt-specific ephemera.

  - Forum Auctions UK – Catalogue 10457 lot 9ba7f860 (signed TSH first) only.

  - Dominic Winter UK – Lot 969 (UK Viking proof) only.

  - Leland Little Auctions (NC) – Lot 6031, September 17, 2025 – Bloomsbury 2009 signed limited box set \#844/1000, ex-Bruce R. Kuniholm collection (Duke University). See §10.1.

The 1992 launch ephemera record is thin in dealer infrastructure beyond the McCaffrey rear-jacket photo, the AP-wire syndication, and the Vanity Fair feature. The 2002 and 2013 launches generated more catalogued ephemera, primarily through the Indiespensable / Foyles / B\&N retail-exclusive programmes. The §8.5 entry below strengthens the 1992 promotional-ephemera record through Knopf's own Fall 1992 seasonal catalog (the Borzoi Reader Vol 4 No 3) containing a pre-publication TSH excerpt.

### 8.5 The Borzoi Reader, Vol. 4 No. 3 (Fall 1992) — Knopf seasonal catalog with TSH pre-publication excerpt

**Imagery** — all four views below are captured in the full 12-page scan at `assets/sources/press_primary/BorzoiReader-Vol4No3-Knopf-Fall1992-CamScanner-full12pp.pdf`:
- **Front cover** — orange/peach autumn maple-leaf design with Borzoi running-dog logo, "Knopf — Volume 4 Number 3 — Fall 1992" label
- **Rear panel** — solid dark olive green; no printing
- **Inside-front-cover spread** — Borzoi Reader masthead, "Fall 1992" date, and "SEE INSIDE BACK COVER" pointer
- **Page 7 spread** — the TSH excerpt with classical-painting illustration, author photograph, and bio caption

**Bibliographic record:**

| Field | Data |
|---|---|
| Title | *The Borzoi Reader* |
| Volume / Issue | **Volume 4, Number 3** |
| Date | **Fall 1992** |
| Publisher | Alfred A. Knopf, Inc. (Borzoi imprint), New York — in-house seasonal catalog |
| Format | Saddle-stitched magazine / catalog; rectangular trade format (approximately octavo to small quarto) |
| Cover design | Orange/peach autumn maple-leaf graphic (overlapping leaf silhouettes in four colorways) with the Knopf Borzoi running-dog logo centered in a pale-green label at top; second pale-green label at bottom reads "Knopf / Volume 4 Number 3 / Fall 1992" |
| Rear panel | Solid dark olive green; unprinted (the title-block-on-rear convention is reversed from typical magazine layout) |
| Spine | Dark olive green (matching rear panel) |
| Interior page-count | Not directly visible from the supplied photographs; the TSH excerpt sits at p. 7 and the magazine appears to run at least to p. 16 (typical Borzoi Reader format) |

**Tartt content — the TSH excerpt:**

- **Location:** p. 7
- **Title block on the excerpt page:** "THE SECRET HISTORY / DONNA TARTT / A novel"
- **Side caption (gutter margin):** "The opening confession of Donna Tartt's astonishing debut novel / SEPTEMBER" — explicit pre-publication framing; the "SEPTEMBER" tag flags TSH as the September 1992 Knopf release
- **Text of the excerpt:** the **opening pages of TSH** beginning *"The snow in the mountains was melting and Bunny had been dead for several weeks before we came to understand the gravity of our situation. He'd been dead for ten days before they found him, you know..."* — this is the Prologue / opening Bunny-manhunt passage that opens the published novel
- **Illustration:** a classical-painting reproduction running across the upper half of the page spread; visually a Lawrence Alma-Tadema / Victorian neoclassical scene (figures in white robes around a reclining woman, classical architecture in background) — chosen by Knopf's art direction to evoke the novel's Greek/classics-academic milieu
- **Author photograph:** a small B&W portrait of Tartt at lower right of the second column (period photograph c.1991–92, consistent with the same photograph used on the §2.3a Uncorrected Proof rear panel)
- **Author bio (caption beneath excerpt):** **"Donna Tartt was born in Mississippi, educated at Bennington College, and lives in New York City. This is her first book."** — this is the cleanest contemporaneous 1992 Tartt bio in any documented promotional artefact, and confirms Tartt as still NYC-based at Fall 1992 (the "Virginia-based" descriptor surfaces only in 2001 Artforum, §7.12)

**Collector significance:**

- **First serial / pre-publication appearance of TSH in print.** The Borzoi Reader Vol 4 No 3 was distributed to booksellers, libraries, and trade reviewers in advance of the September 16, 1992 publication date. The opening passage of TSH therefore appeared in print in the Borzoi Reader **before** the trade first edition. This is the earliest documented printed appearance of TSH text in this reference — preceding even the §2.3a Uncorrected Proof in distribution sequence, given that seasonal catalogs ship ahead of bound proofs.
- **Knopf's own promotional artefact.** Unlike third-party magazine coverage (Vanity Fair, Esquire, Newsweek, etc. — §8.1, §8.4), this is publisher-produced material — Knopf marketing TSH directly to the trade. It is the missing piece of the 1992 promotional ephemera record.
- **Resolves the §8.4 note.** §8.4 had noted that no catalogued Knopf in-house promotional booklet featuring TSH had been located; this entry supplies it.
- **Text-comparison opportunity.** The Borzoi Reader excerpt can be collated against the trade first to check whether the opening Bunny-manhunt passage carried any pre-publication text variants (Cochrane epigraph swap precedent — §2.3 parent). From the visible photograph, the prose appears very close to the published opening, but a side-by-side reading would confirm. If textual variants exist, this excerpt becomes a bibliographically more significant Tartt artefact.
- **Tier 1 primary source** for the 1992 promotional strategy. Confirms that Knopf positioned TSH as a "September" lead title in the Fall 1992 list, used classical-art accompaniment for the excerpt, and was already framing the novel with the "opening confession" / "astonishing debut" marketing language six weeks before publication.

**Authentication notes:**

- The Borzoi Reader was Knopf's seasonal in-house catalog throughout the 1980s and 1990s; Volume 4 Number 3 = Fall 1992 places it correctly in the sequence (if quarterly from a 1989 launch, Vol 4 = 1992; if other intervals, verify against other Borzoi Reader issues from the period).
- Knopf Borzoi running-dog logo on cover is the period-correct design — matches the same colophon on §2.3a (Uncorrected Proof rear panel) and §2.1 (trade first dust jacket).
- "SEE INSIDE BACK COVER" pointer on the inside-front-cover spread is typical Borzoi Reader layout — suggesting the back inside cover carries title/subscription/ordering information.
- Classical-painting illustration is unsigned in the supplied photograph; identifying the specific painting and artist would add another data point to the cataloguing (likely Alma-Tadema, Frederic Leighton, or a similar Victorian neoclassical painter — Knopf's library of stock imagery for the period).

**Saved Assets (§8.5):**
- **Full 12-page PDF scan of the in-hand copy:** `assets/sources/press_primary/BorzoiReader-Vol4No3-Knopf-Fall1992-CamScanner-full12pp.pdf` — covers, both fly-leaves with the Easton Press tipped-in promo, the contents page (TOC), the TSH excerpt at p. 7, and the credits/colophon back panel.

## 9. Authentication

### 9.1 Tartt signature characteristics by era

![Figure 9.1 — A characteristic Tartt-signed copy of The Secret History (US Knopf 1992 first edition) inscribed by Tartt on the half-title "To Diana — Warm regards, Donna Tartt" AND additionally signed by jacket designer Chip Kidd on the front jacket panel. Note Tartt's flowing horizontal stroke through the signature line. Inscription style is typical: short, with "warm regards" salutation, recipient's first name, signed full name. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (ABAA, T2)](assets/images/rId69.jpg "Figure 9.1 — A characteristic Tartt-signed copy of The Secret History (US Knopf 1992 first edition) inscribed by Tartt on the half-title \"To Diana — Warm regards, Donna Tartt\" AND additionally signed by jacket designer Chip Kidd on the front jacket panel. Note Tartt's flowing horizontal stroke through the signature line. Inscription style is typical: short, with \"warm regards\" salutation, recipient's first name, signed full name. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (ABAA, T2)")

Figure 9.1 — A characteristic Tartt-signed copy of The Secret History (US Knopf 1992 first edition) inscribed by Tartt on the half-title "To Diana — Warm regards, Donna Tartt" AND additionally signed by jacket designer Chip Kidd on the front jacket panel. Note Tartt's flowing horizontal stroke through the signature line. Inscription style is typical: short, with "warm regards" salutation, recipient's first name, signed full name. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (ABAA, T2)

*Figure 9.1 — A characteristic Tartt-signed copy of The Secret History (US Knopf 1992 first edition) inscribed by Tartt on the half-title "To Diana — Warm regards, Donna Tartt" AND additionally signed by jacket designer Chip Kidd on the front jacket panel. Note Tartt's flowing horizontal stroke through the signature line. Inscription style is typical: short, with "warm regards" salutation, recipient's first name, signed full name. Photo: Raptis Rare Books (ABAA, T2)*

Tartt signs in a flowing hand. Across eras (1992 / 2002 / 2013 / 2020s) the signature is consistent in legibility and pressure. Inscriptions are usually short — "To [name] — warm regards, Donna Tartt" is the modal form, with variants "warmest regards" or "with all warm regards." Authentic signatures show no hesitation strokes; the loop of the "D" in "Donna" connects fluidly to the hairline downstroke into "Tartt."

### 9.2 Ink colours used in signing programs (key authentication tool)

| | | |
| ----------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------ |
| **Edition / program** | **Ink colour** | **Source** |
| Personal signing & inscriptions across her career (general) | Brown ink (common) | Multiple ABAA descriptions |
| Bloomsbury 2009 boxed signed limited (TSH + TLF) | Venetian ink | Bloomsbury / dealer descriptions [1] |
| UK Little, Brown 2013 deluxe signed limited (Goldfinch) | Blue ink | dpsbs.com \#310/1000; Sotheby's \#574/1000 [20] |
| Foyles 2013 signed first edition (Goldfinch) | Copper ink | Multiple dealer descriptions |
| Powell's Indiespensable Vol. 43 (Goldfinch, 2013) | Purple ink | Powell's product page; dealer descriptions [77] |
| Viking 2022 30th Anniversary signed limited (TSH) | Limitation page printed (ink not specified) | Biblio listing |
| Folio Society 2023 signed limited (Jackson, *We Have Always Lived in the Castle*) — 500 numbered + 20 lettered HC | **Black ink** (medium nib, on bright-orange colophon stock) | §7.14; collector-supplied photo of copy #442 |

A copy claiming to be from one of these signing programs whose ink colour does not match the program's standard should be regarded with skepticism. The above is the most useful single tool for authenticating signed Tartt copies.

**Folio Society 2023 signature characteristics:** The Tartt signature on copy #442 shows the late-period Tartt letterforms — looped capital D with small inner closure; the "T" in Tartt with a horizontal crossbar that extends across into the doubled-t (second t crossbar continues from the first); no underline; consistent slant ~12° to right; full surname spelled out (not just "DT" initials). Pen evidently a fine-to-medium gel or rollerball depositing solid black ink with no significant variation in line weight — consistent with the Folio Society's customary signing-pen choice for their limited editions. The bright orange of the colophon stock plus the firm black ink produces a high-contrast plate that is well-suited for authentication comparison.

### 9.3 Common inscription phrases

"warmest regards," "warm regards," "with all warm regards," "best wishes." Inscribed copies typically carry the recipient's first name. Greek-language inscriptions are not in the public record.

### 9.4 Forgery red flags

  - Signature without inscription on a copy supposedly from a personal-signing programme

  - Ink colour wrong for the signing programme (per §9.2)

  - A B\&N-style bookplate that appears to be photocopied or laser-printed onto the half-title rather than tipped in

  - Powell's Indiespensable copy missing its slipcase or chapbook companion

  - Bloomsbury 2009 boxed set without the slipcase or with a number out of the 1–1,000 series

  - Counterfeit Knopf 1992 first/first acetate jackets do exist; verify against confirmed photos

### 9.5 Reputable dealers with Tartt material

  - Peter Harrington (London, NYC) — ABA / ILAB / PBFA / LAPADA

  - Bauman Rare Books (NY, Las Vegas, Philadelphia) — ABAA

  - Raptis Rare Books (Palm Beach) — ABAA

  - Type Punch Matrix — ABAA

  - MintFirsts — ABAA

  - Quill & Brush — ABAA

  - Second Story Books — ABAA

  - Lorne Bair Rare Books — ABAA

  - James Cummins Bookseller — ABAA

  - Heritage Book Shop — ABAA

  - Whitmore Rare Books — ABAA

  - Captain Ahab's Rare Books — ABAA

  - Maggs Bros. (UK) — ABA / ILAB

  - Jonkers Rare Books (Henley-on-Thames) — ABA / PBFA / ILAB

  - Sue Lloyd-Davies Books (UK, deluxe limiteds)

  - Between the Covers Rare Books (NJ) — ABAA

  - Grayshelf Books (TX) — ABAA, IOBA

  - Evening Star Books (WI) — ABAA / ILAB

  - Yesterday's Gallery (CT) — ABAA

  - Sotheby's Buy Now Marketplace (modern firsts)

Aggregate observation: 19 sold lots traced via Barnebys + 3 Heritage lots + 7 PBA Galleries lots + 2 Dominic Winter lots + 1 Forum lot + 1 Leland Little lot = 33+ documented Tartt auction lots over 22 years (2004-2026). Realised prices range from $15 (Heritage Oct 2010 — pre-Pulitzer floor for signed TSH first) to $5,090+ (Catawiki Feb 2016, 20-volume Bezige Bij set including Tartt) and $23,606 (Catawiki April 2015 photo-book including Tartt portrait — the photo-book, not Tartt material specifically, drove that price).

The pre-Pulitzer (April 2014) floor for signed TSH first auction prices is documented at $15-$32 for Heritage and Bloomsbury Auctions in 2010. Post-Pulitzer (April 2014 onward) signed TSH first auction prices are notably higher. The TLF 2002 ARC \#130/940 sold for $1,786 in 2016 — substantially higher than typical TLF first hardcover prices, reflecting the 940-copy signed pre-publication state's rarity.

Coverage limitations: Heritage Auctions blocks automated retrieval, so the Heritage-archive search relied on search snippets rather than direct catalogue retrieval. Christie's, Swann, Bonhams, PBA Galleries, and Forum Auctions were searched directly via their archive interfaces; only the entries above appeared. Tartt material at the major-house level is relatively sparse; the secondary market for Tartt's books moves predominantly through ABAA / ILAB / ABA / PBFA antiquarian channels. For Tartt manuscript material, see §10.2 below.

### 10.2 Association copies, manuscripts, and correspondence in private hands

Documented association copies:

  - Author + Chip Kidd (jacket designer) dual-signed copies of The Secret History.

  - Author + Bret Easton Ellis (dedicatee) dual-signed TSH ARC – surfaced via Barnebys aggregator (lot vqjmvlfwjj). Inscribed by Tartt on title page; signed by Ellis on the dedication page. The dual-signed-by-author-and-dedicatee state is the rarest TSH ARC variant.

  - Square Books, Oxford, MS – September 17, 1992 launch signing (Tartt's hometown bookstore). November 14, 2002 TLF Thacker Mountain Radio Show signing (flyer in Ole Miss MUM00441).

  - Pre-publication inscribed copies – proof and ARC states are signed regularly; the most significant primary-source pre-publication inscription documented is the Captain Ahab's TSH inscribed to Otto Penzler dated 9/10/92 (six days pre-publication) – a provenance link to the 1996 Penzler “True Crime” poem.

  - Bound manuscript copy of The Secret History – described as having belonged to Tartt's editor Gary Fisketjon, then passed to Carl Navarre. Signed by Tartt. Offered by Books-4-Ewe Used & Rare Books. The most notable bound-manuscript artefact of Tartt to surface in the open dealer record.

Manuscript / correspondence holdings outside Ole Miss — expanded survey:

  - Bret Easton Ellis literary archive – survey result: negative. No catalogued Bret Easton Ellis Papers identified at Yale Beinecke, NYU Fales (the natural home given Ellis's New York residency), USC Cinematic Arts (where Ellis is associated through film/TV work), or Bennington College alumni archive. Ellis's papers, if formally archived anywhere, have not been catalogued in finding aids accessible via OCLC ArchiveGrid as of 2026. Tartt-Ellis Bennington-era correspondence (manuscript exchanges documented through Once Upon a Time at Bennington College podcast interviews) therefore remains in private hands.

  - Allen Tate Papers – surveys of the Allen Tate Papers at Princeton Library Special Collections and the Allen Tate-related material at Vanderbilt did not surface catalogued Tartt correspondence. No record located.

  - Willie Morris Papers – Tartt's tribute essay “My friend, my mentor, my inspiration” (Remembering Willie, 2000; §6.4) implies an active correspondence; the Willie Morris Collection at the University of Mississippi (separate accession from MUM00441 Tartt SMMSS) and at Yale Beinecke was searched. No record located – no catalogued Tartt letters surfaced.

  - Barry Hannah Papers – Tartt's Bennington / Mississippi creative-writing mentor. The Barry Hannah Papers at the University of Mississippi were searched; none identified for catalogued Tartt correspondence (informal correspondence may exist in unprocessed material).

  - Lili Anolik Bennington oral-history project – extensive interviews conducted 2019-2021 across Esquire (“The Secret Oral History of Bennington: The 1980s' Most Decadent College,” 2019), Vanity Fair, and the podcast Once Upon a Time… at Bennington College (2020-2021). Anolik's interviews reference Tartt-Ellis manuscript exchanges from Bennington but do not catalogue or quote any Tartt letter or manuscript page. Tartt's literary agents sent legal warnings to Apple Podcasts and to the podcast creators, citing concerns over potential use of Tartt's published works without permission, of her private school records, or of “false, misleading or otherwise inaccurate” statements about her. The legal warnings did not pull the podcast from publication; episodes remain available on Apple, Spotify, and Audible. The Anolik archive is a secondary-source oral-history record rather than a primary-source manuscript collection.

Auction-house manuscript / correspondence searches:

  - Heritage Auctions Manuscripts – search returned no Tartt T.L.S. or autograph letter.

  - Christie's Books & Manuscripts – no Tartt material.

  - Sotheby's Books & Manuscripts – no Tartt material (the Sotheby's Buy Now Marketplace Goldfinch UK Deluxe is a fixed-price retail listing, not a manuscript auction).

  - Bonhams Books & Manuscripts – no Tartt material.

  - Swann Manuscripts – no Tartt material.

  - Forum Auctions UK / Dominic Winter – only the items in §10.1.

Conclusion: Tartt manuscript and correspondence material in the open auction / dealer market is essentially limited to (a) the Books-4-Ewe Fisketjon→Navarre bound manuscript copy, (b) the Captain Ahab's pre-publication Penzler inscription, and (c) signed first editions and association copies through ABAA channels. No formal Tartt papers archive exists outside Ole Miss MUM00441.

### 10.6 Documented Tartt signing events

Tartt has been notably averse to book tours throughout her career. In a 2013 Irish Independent interview, she stated that she dislikes going on book tours and giving talks because she finds them mentally exhausting [68]. Per Tartt at her 2013 Cambridge Wordfest appearance, that event was her “third talk in England in the past eleven years” — substantiating the sparse-event record [69].

Documented signing events (auctioneer records / contemporaneous press / publisher records / event venue confirmations):

| | | | | | |
| ------------- | --------- | ------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Date** | **Novel** | **Venue** | **Host / partner** | **Form of signing** | **Source** |
| Sept 17, 1992 | TSH | Square Books, Oxford MS | Tartt's hometown bookstore | Open signing of trade firsts; canonical TSH launch event | §10.2 [70] |
| 1992-93 | TSH | Knopf Borzoi tour | Knopf publicity | Tour schedule existed at randomhouse.com/knopf/authors/tartt/tour.html (Wayback retrieval needed) | [71] |
